The Five Universals
beginner
5 min
Dividing the Universal: Essential, Accidental, Intermediate
Explains the division of the universal into three types based on the matn line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given universal as essential, accidental, or intermediate based on its relation to the substance (dhat).

Core Idea
The universal is divided by its relation to the thing's substance: inside, outside, or identical.

This lesson introduces a fundamental classification in logic: the division of the universal (kulli) into three types based on its relation to the substance (dhat). The passage explains how the matn line implies this division. Understanding this classification is key to constructing accurate definitions and avoiding errors in reasoning across Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Recognize that the universal is divided into essential (dhati), accidental (aradi), and intermediate (wasita). These are the three categories derived from the matn.
2
Understand the criterion
The division depends on whether the universal falls within the substance (essential), exits from it (accidental), or is identical to it (intermediate). The matn says 'if it falls within the substance, then attribute it; or for the accidental, when it exits.'
3
Apply the criterion to examples
For 'human': 'animal' is essential (part of definition), 'white' is accidental (outside substance), and 'human' itself is intermediate (identical to the substance).
The species is the intermediate because it is the substance itself.
4
Note the implication from the matn
The author's phrase implies the intermediate by excluding it from the first two. The species is neither inside nor outside but identical, making it the intermediate.
This shows how logical divisions are extracted from concise expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلاً لِلذَّاتِ إِنْ فِيهَا انْدَرَجُ فَانْسِبْهُ، أَوْ لِعَارِضِ إِذَا خَرَجْ. غَرَضُ المُصَنِّفِ بِذَلِكَ : تَقْسِيمُ الكُلِّيّ : إِلَى ذَاتِيُّ، وَإِلَى عَرَضِيٌّ، وَإِلَى وَاسِطَةٍ . وَهَذَا مَأخُودٌ (٢) مِنْ كَلَامِهِ بِطَرِيقِ المَنْهُوم ; حَيْثُ قَيَّدَ الأَوَّلَ» بـ «الإِنْدِرَاجِ فِي الذَّاتِ», وَالثَّانِي بِالخُرُوجِ عَنْهَا , فَيُعْلَمُ مِنْهُ أَنَّ النَّوْعَ وَاسِطَةٌ ; لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْدَرجُ فِي الذَّاتِ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجْ عَنْهَا , بَلْ هُوَ عَيْنُهَا، وَهُوَ أَحَدُ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ ثَلَاثَةٍ اشْتُهِرَتْ مِنِ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ فِي ذَلِكَ . ثَانِيهَا : أَنَّ الذَّاتِيَّ : مَا انْدَرَجَ فِي الذَّاتِ وَالعَرَضِيَّ : مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ», وَعَلَيْهِ فَالنَّوْعُ عَرَضِيٌّ (۳). (۱) الشرشيمي : قوله : (مَا لَا يَمْنَعُ نَفْسُ تَصَوُّرِهِ) أي : لفظ لا يمنع نفس تصور معناه من وقوع الشَّركة فيه، وإنما قلنا : «لفظ» ولم نوقع «ما» على «معنى» ; لأجل مناسبته لكلام المصنِّف مِن أنَّ التَّقسيم للفظ , لا للمعنى، وإن كان بواسطة المعنى، وإنما زاد لفظ «نفس»، ولم يقل : «تصوره» ; إشارة إلى أنَّ منع التّصور وقوع الشَّركة فيه بالنَّظر للجزئي، وعدم منعه وقوع الشركة فيه بالنظر للكلِّي باعتبار التصور نفسه، وقطع النظر عن الخارجي; ألا ترى أنَّ «الإله» بمعنى: «المعبود بحق» يمنع تصور مفهومه باعتبار الدليل الخارجي ; كقوله تعالى : لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا وَالِمَةٌ إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَنَا) [الأنبياء : ٢٢] وقوع الشركة فيه (۲) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَهَذَا مَاخُوذُ أي : التَّقسيم إلى ثلاثة أقسام، أو الإشارة إلى الواسطة، وذكر اسم الإشارة باعتبار المذكور، وهذا هو المتعين كما يُعلم من آخر عبارته . (3) الشرشيمي : قوله : (فَالنَّوْعُ عَرَضِيٌّ) والنسبةُ على هذا من نسبة اللَّازم إلى الملزوم ; لأنَّه يلزم مِنَ الصَّحك» مثلاً حقيقة الإنسان» التي هي حَيَوَان نَاطِق».
And first, for the essential, if it falls within the substance, then attribute it; or for the accidental, when it exits. The author's purpose by that is the division of the universal into essential, accidental, and intermediate. And this is taken from his speech by way of implication, since he restricted the first to 'falling within the substance' and the second to 'exiting from it', so it is known from that that the species is an intermediate, because it does not fall within the substance nor exit from it, but rather it is the very substance itself. And this is one of three terminologies that became famous among many terminologies in that. The second of them: that the essential is what falls within the substance, and the accidental is what is not like that, and accordingly the species is accidental. Al-Shirshimi said: His saying 'what the very conception of it does not prevent the occurrence of sharing in it' means: an expression the very conception of its meaning does not prevent the occurrence of sharing in it. And we said 'expression' and did not place 'what' upon 'meaning' for the sake of appropriateness to the author's speech that the division is for the expression, not for the meaning, although by mediation of the meaning. And he added the word 'very' and did not say 'its conception' to indicate that the prevention of conception of the occurrence of sharing in it is with respect to the particular, and the non-prevention of the occurrence of sharing in it is with respect to the universal considering the conception itself, disregarding external evidence; do you not see that 'al-Ilah' meaning 'the one truly worshipped' prevents the conception of its meaning, considering external evidence like His saying: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' [al-Anbiya:22], the occurrence of sharing in it. Al-Shirshimi: His saying 'and this is taken' means: the division into three divisions, or the reference to the intermediate, and the demonstrative pronoun refers to what was mentioned, and this is the appropriate as known from the end of his statement. Al-Shirshimi: His saying 'so the species is accidental' and the relation according to this is that of the necessary to the necessary, because from 'laughing' for example the reality of 'human' which is rational animal is entailed.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides an explanation of a matn line from al-Sullam that divides the universal into three types: essential (dhati), accidental (aradi), and intermediate (wasita). The matn line says: 'And first, for the essential, if it falls within the substance, then attribute it; or for the accidental, when it exits.' Al-Bajuri explains that the author's purpose is to divide the universal into these three. The division is derived from the matn by implication: if something falls within the substance, it is essential; if it exits (i.e., is outside the substance), it is accidental; and what is neither inside nor outside but identical to the substance is the species, which is the intermediate. Al-Bajuri notes that this is one of three well-known terminologies. The second terminology holds that the essential is what falls within the substance and the accidental is what is not like that, making the species accidental. The marginal note by al-Shirshimi further clarifies the definition of the particular (from a previous context) and discusses the relation of the species to the accidental. This lesson is important for understanding how universals are classified in logic, which is foundational to constructing definitions and proofs.

The Species: Intermediate or Accidental? Two Terminologies
Discusses two terminologies regarding the classification of the species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two terminologies regarding the species and explain why it is considered intermediate in one and accidental in another.

Core Idea
The species is identical to the substance, so in one terminology it is intermediate, while in another it is accidental because it is not a part.

This lesson delves into the variations in classifying universals. The passage mentions two terminologies: in the first, the species is intermediate; in the second, it is accidental. Understanding this variation is crucial for reading classical texts where different authors may use different conventions. The super-commentary by al-Shirshimi explains the logical relation in the second terminology.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the first terminology
In the first terminology, the species is intermediate because it is the very substance itself, not a part. This is the view presented in the matn implication.
The species (e.g., 'human') is identical to the substance, so it is neither inside nor outside.
2
Understand the second terminology
The second terminology defines essential as what falls within the substance. Since the species does not fall within (it is the whole), it is considered accidental.
Here, 'essential' is only what is a constituent part; the whole is not essential but accidental by this definition.
3
Identify the implication
In the second terminology, all universals that are not parts of the definition are called accidental. This includes species, genera beyond the immediate, and accidents proper.
4
Note the super-commentator's clarification
Al-Shirshimi explains that the relation in the second terminology is that of the necessary to the necessary: from 'laughing' the reality of 'human' is entailed. This shows that the species (human) necessarily follows from a property (laughing), making it accidental in that terminology.
This logical relation reinforces why the species is considered accidental: it is not a part but a necessary concomitant.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلاً لِلذَّاتِ إِنْ فِيهَا انْدَرَجُ فَانْسِبْهُ، أَوْ لِعَارِضِ إِذَا خَرَجْ. غَرَضُ المُصَنِّفِ بِذَلِكَ : تَقْسِيمُ الكُلِّيّ : إِلَى ذَاتِيُّ، وَإِلَى عَرَضِيٌّ، وَإِلَى وَاسِطَةٍ . وَهَذَا مَأخُودٌ (٢) مِنْ كَلَامِهِ بِطَرِيقِ المَنْهُوم ; حَيْثُ قَيَّدَ الأَوَّلَ» بـ «الإِنْدِرَاجِ فِي الذَّاتِ», وَالثَّانِي بِالخُرُوجِ عَنْهَا , فَيُعْلَمُ مِنْهُ أَنَّ النَّوْعَ وَاسِطَةٌ ; لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْدَرجُ فِي الذَّاتِ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجْ عَنْهَا , بَلْ هُوَ عَيْنُهَا، وَهُوَ أَحَدُ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ ثَلَاثَةٍ اشْتُهِرَتْ مِنِ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ فِي ذَلِكَ . ثَانِيهَا : أَنَّ الذَّاتِيَّ : مَا انْدَرَجَ فِي الذَّاتِ وَالعَرَضِيَّ : مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ», وَعَلَيْهِ فَالنَّوْعُ عَرَضِيٌّ (۳). (۱) الشرشيمي : قوله : (مَا لَا يَمْنَعُ نَفْسُ تَصَوُّرِهِ) أي : لفظ لا يمنع نفس تصور معناه من وقوع الشَّركة فيه، وإنما قلنا : «لفظ» ولم نوقع «ما» على «معنى» ; لأجل مناسبته لكلام المصنِّف مِن أنَّ التَّقسيم للفظ , لا للمعنى، وإن كان بواسطة المعنى، وإنما زاد لفظ «نفس»، ولم يقل : «تصوره» ; إشارة إلى أنَّ منع التّصور وقوع الشَّركة فيه بالنَّظر للجزئي، وعدم منعه وقوع الشركة فيه بالنظر للكلِّي باعتبار التصور نفسه، وقطع النظر عن الخارجي; ألا ترى أنَّ «الإله» بمعنى: «المعبود بحق» يمنع تصور مفهومه باعتبار الدليل الخارجي ; كقوله تعالى : لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا وَالِمَةٌ إِلَّا اللهُ لَفَسَدَنَا) [الأنبياء : ٢٢] وقوع الشركة فيه (۲) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَهَذَا مَاخُوذُ أي : التَّقسيم إلى ثلاثة أقسام، أو الإشارة إلى الواسطة، وذكر اسم الإشارة باعتبار المذكور، وهذا هو المتعين كما يُعلم من آخر عبارته . (3) الشرشيمي : قوله : (فَالنَّوْعُ عَرَضِيٌّ) والنسبةُ على هذا من نسبة اللَّازم إلى الملزوم ; لأنَّه يلزم مِنَ الصَّحك» مثلاً حقيقة الإنسان» التي هي حَيَوَان نَاطِق».
And first, for the essential, if it falls within the substance, then attribute it; or for the accidental, when it exits. The author's purpose by that is the division of the universal into essential, accidental, and intermediate. And this is taken from his speech by way of implication, since he restricted the first to 'falling within the substance' and the second to 'exiting from it', so it is known from that that the species is an intermediate, because it does not fall within the substance nor exit from it, but rather it is the very substance itself. And this is one of three terminologies that became famous among many terminologies in that. The second of them: that the essential is what falls within the substance, and the accidental is what is not like that, and accordingly the species is accidental. Al-Shirshimi said: His saying 'what the very conception of it does not prevent the occurrence of sharing in it' means: an expression the very conception of its meaning does not prevent the occurrence of sharing in it. And we said 'expression' and did not place 'what' upon 'meaning' for the sake of appropriateness to the author's speech that the division is for the expression, not for the meaning, although by mediation of the meaning. And he added the word 'very' and did not say 'its conception' to indicate that the prevention of conception of the occurrence of sharing in it is with respect to the particular, and the non-prevention of the occurrence of sharing in it is with respect to the universal considering the conception itself, disregarding external evidence; do you not see that 'al-Ilah' meaning 'the one truly worshipped' prevents the conception of its meaning, considering external evidence like His saying: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' [al-Anbiya:22], the occurrence of sharing in it. Al-Shirshimi: His saying 'and this is taken' means: the division into three divisions, or the reference to the intermediate, and the demonstrative pronoun refers to what was mentioned, and this is the appropriate as known from the end of his statement. Al-Shirshimi: His saying 'so the species is accidental' and the relation according to this is that of the necessary to the necessary, because from 'laughing' for example the reality of 'human' which is rational animal is entailed.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides an explanation of a matn line from al-Sullam that divides the universal into three types: essential (dhati), accidental (aradi), and intermediate (wasita). The matn line says: 'And first, for the essential, if it falls within the substance, then attribute it; or for the accidental, when it exits.' Al-Bajuri explains that the author's purpose is to divide the universal into these three. The division is derived from the matn by implication: if something falls within the substance, it is essential; if it exits (i.e., is outside the substance), it is accidental; and what is neither inside nor outside but identical to the substance is the species, which is the intermediate. Al-Bajuri notes that this is one of three well-known terminologies. The second terminology holds that the essential is what falls within the substance and the accidental is what is not like that, making the species accidental. The marginal note by al-Shirshimi further clarifies the definition of the particular (from a previous context) and discusses the relation of the species to the accidental. This lesson is important for understanding how universals are classified in logic, which is foundational to constructing definitions and proofs.

العرضي
النوع
الذاتي

Key Takeaway
The classification of the species varies across terminologies: in one it is intermediate (identical to substance), in another accidental (not a part).

Real vs. Relative Particular and Affirmation/Negation
Author explains why kulli is defined affirmatively and juz'i negatively, and distinguishes haqiqi from idafi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real particular (juz'i haqiqi) and relative particular (juz'i idafi), and explain why the universal is defined affirmatively and the particular negatively.

Core Idea
The particular is not just the individual; relative particularity is a conceptual relation.

In this passage, al-Bajuri explains two important points: why the universal is defined by affirmation and the particular by negation, and the two types of particular. These distinctions are essential for precise definitions in Islamic sciences, especially when classifying terms in usul al-fiqh and kalam. We will unpack the reasoning and apply it to examples.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two reasons for affirmation/negation
Identify in the text the two reasons al-Bajuri gives: (1) affirmation is nobler (ashraf) than negation, and (2) negation of a thing cannot be conceived without first understanding its existence. These justify defining the universal affirmatively and the particular negatively.
Note that reason 2 applies specifically to defining the particular by negation, not to the universal.
2
Understand why reason 1 applies to both definitions
Al-Bajuri mentions that the first reason (affirmation is nobler) explains why another scholar who defined the universal by negation still began with affirmation (that scholar defined universal as 'what does not prevent sharing', which is a negation but implies prior affirmation). The second reason does not apply to that definition because it does not define the particular negatively.
This shows the importance of context in evaluating definitions.
3
Distinguish real particular from relative particular
The real particular (juz'i haqiqi) is what cannot be predicated of many (e.g., Zayd). The relative particular (juz'i idafi) is what falls under a more general concept (e.g., 'man' relative to 'animal'). They combine in individuals: Zayd is both real (as an individual) and relative (as a human). But 'man' is only relative, not real, because it can be predicated of many.
Memorize the definitions: haqiqi = prevents sharing; idafi = falls under broader concept.
4
Test with examples
Apply the distinction: Take 'Zayd' – can it be predicated of many? No, so it is real. Does it fall under something more general? Yes, 'human', so it is also relative. Take 'human' – can it be predicated of many? Yes, so it is not real. Does it fall under something more general? Yes, 'animal', so it is relative. This clarifies the overlap.
Practice with other terms like 'animal', 'Hasan', 'horse'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِأَنَّهُ قَدْ عَرَّفَ الكُلِّيَّ بِالإِيجَابِ، وَالجُزْئِيَّ بِالسَّلْبِ، وَالإِيجَابُ أَشْرَفُ مِنَ السَّلْبِ، وَأَيْضاً : سَلْبُ الشَّيْءِ لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ إِلَّا بَعْدَ تَعَقُلِ وُجُودِهِ. وَبِالوَجْهِ الأَوَّلِ يُوَجَّهُ تَقْدِيمُ غَيْرِ المُصَنِّفِ لِذَلِكَ ، لَا بِالوَجْهِ الثَّانِي ؛ لِأَنَّ غَيْرَ الْمُصَنِّفِ إِنَّمَا عَرَّفَ الكُلِّيَّ بِالسَّلْبِ حَيْثُ قَالَ: مَا لَا يَمْنَعُ نَفْسُ تَصَوُّرِهِ مِنْ وُقُوعِ الشَّرِكَةِ فِيهِ (۱) وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ كَلَامَ المُصَنِّفِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي الجُزْئِيِّ الحَقِيقِيِّ ، وَأَمَّا الجُزْئِيُّ الإِضَافِيُّ فَهُوَ : «مَا انْدَرَجَ تَحْتَ مَا هُوَ أَعَمُّ مِنْهُ ، وَبَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الحَقِيقِيّ : العُمُومُ وَالخُصُوصُ بِإِطْلَاقِ، فَيَجْتَمِعَانِ فِي «زَيْدِ» مَثَلاً، وَيَنْفَرِدُ الإِضَافِيُّ فِي نَحْوِ الإِنْسَانِ».
And because he defined the universal by affirmation, and the particular by negation, and affirmation is nobler than negation, and also: negation of a thing is not conceived except after understanding its existence. And by the first aspect is justified the ordering of other than the author for that, not by the second aspect; because other than the author defined the universal by negation where he said: 'What the conception of its meaning itself does not prevent the occurrence of sharing in it.' And know that the author's statement is only concerning the real particular (juz'i haqiqi). As for the relative particular (juz'i idafi), it is: 'What falls under what is more general than it.' And between it and the real particular is absolute generality and specificity, so they combine in 'Zayd' for example, and the relative particular is unique in something like 'man'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note on the matn line about the universal. The author (al-Bajuri) gives reasons why the universal is defined by affirmation and the particular by negation: first, affirmation is nobler, second, negation presupposes existence. Then he notes that another scholar (possibly the author of the matn? Actually 'other than the author' refers to someone else) defined the universal by negation, so his ordering is explained by the first reason only. Then he distinguishes two types of particular: haqiqi (real) and idafi (relative). The real particular cannot be predicated of many, like Zayd. The relative particular is something that falls under a more general concept, like 'man' which is particular relative to 'animal' but universal relative to individuals. He gives examples: Zayd is both real and relative (as a human), while 'man' is only relative (not real).

Key Terms
الجُزْئِيُّ الحَقِيقِيُّ
الجُزْئِيُّ الإِضَافِيُّ

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why is the universal defined by affirmation and the particular by negation?
A) Because affirmation is nobler and negation cannot be conceived without prior affirmation.
B) Because the universal is more general than the particular.
C) Because the author prefers affirmation over negation.
D) Because the particular is easier to define by negation.

Key Takeaway
The universal is defined affirmatively and the particular negatively for two reasons: nobility of affirmation and the dependence of negation on existence; additionally, the particular is of two types: real (haqiqi) and relative (idafi).

8 min
The Three Conventions for Essential and Accidental
Author explains three conventions for dividing universals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three conventions for classifying universals as essential (dhati) or accidental (aradi), and correctly determine the status of the species (naw) under each convention.

Core Idea
The species is the whole essence, but its classification depends on which convention you adopt.

In logic, the division of universals into essential (dhati) and accidental (aradi) is not fixed. Different logicians adopt different conventions, especially regarding the species (naw). This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies three famous conventions. By learning them, you will see how the same universal—the species—can be classified as intermediate, accidental, or essential depending on the convention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the division of universals
Read the first part of the passage where the author says the universal is divided into three: essential (included in the essence), accidental (outside the essence), and intermediate (neither included nor outside).
2
Understand the first convention (species as intermediate)
The matn implies that the species is intermediate because it is neither a part of the essence nor outside it, but the essence itself. This is the first convention: species is wasit (intermediate).
This is the convention adopted by the matn author.
3
Understand the second convention (species as accidental)
Here, 'essential' means what is included in the essence. Since the species is not a part (it is the whole), it is not included, so it is accidental. Thus the species is 'aradi under this convention.
4
Understand the third convention (species as essential)
Here, 'accidental' means what is outside the essence. Since the species is not outside (it is the essence itself), it is not accidental, so it is essential (dhati).
These three conventions show the flexibility of terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (وَأَوَّلاً ... إلخ) غَرَضُ المُصَنِّفِ بِذَلِكَ : تَقْسِيمُ الكُلِّيّ : إِلَى ذَاتِيٌّ، وَإِلَى عَرَضِيٌّ، وَإِلَى وَاسِطَةٍ . وَهَذَا مَأْخُوذٌ مِنْ كَلَامِهِ بِطَرِيقِ المَفْهُومِ ؛ حَيْثُ قَيَّدَ الأَوَّلَ بـ «الإِنْدِرَاجِ فِي الذَّاتِ»، وَالثَّانِي بِالخُرُوجِ عَنْهَا ، فَيُعْلَمُ مِنْهُ أَنَّ النَّوْعَ وَاسِطَةٌ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْدَرِجُ فِي الذَّاتِ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجْ عَنْهَا ، بَلْ هُوَ عَيْنُهَا، وَهُوَ أَحَدُ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ ثَلَاثَةٍ اشْتُهِرَتْ مِنِ اصْطِلَاحَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ فِي ذَلِكَ . ثَانِيهَا : أَنَّ الذَّاتِيَّ : مَا انْدَرَجَ فِي الذَّاتِ وَالعَرَضِيَّ : مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَالنَّوْعُ عَرَضِيٌّ . ثَالِثُهَا : أَنَّ العَرَضِيَ : مَا خَرَجَ عَنِ الذَّاتِ، وَالذَّاتِيَّ : مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَالنَّوْعُ ذَاتِيٌّ . وَتَوْضِيحُ ذَلِكَ : أَنَّ الكُلِّيَّ : - إِمَّا مُنْدَرِجُ فِي الذَّاتِ ؛ بِأَنْ كَانَ جُزْءاً مِنْهَا ، وَهُوَ : الجِنْسُ ، وَالفَصْلُ . - وَإِمَّا خَارِجٌ عَنْهَا ؛ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ جُزْءاً مِنْهَا وَلَا عَيْنَهَا ، وَهُوَ : الخَاصَّةُ، وَالعَرَضُ العَامُ . - وَإِمَّا غَيْرُ مُنْدَرِجِ وَغَيْرُ خَارِج؛ بِأَنْ كَانَ تَمَامَ الذَّاتِ، وَهُوَ : النَّوْعُ . فَالذَّاتُ بِمَعْنَى المَاهِيَّةِ كَـ : «الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الإِنْسَانُ» ، وَالمُنْدَرِجُ فِيهَا كَـ : «الحَيَوَانُ» وَكَ: «النَّاطِقُ، وَالخَارِجُ عَنْهَا كَ: الضَّاحِكُ وَكَ: «المَاشِي، وَغَيْرُ المُنْدَرِجِ وَغَيْرُ الخَارِجِ ـ «الإِنْسَانُ»، وَلَا يَخْفَى عَلَيْكَ تَنْزِيلُ الخِلَافِ المَذْكُورِ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ .
His statement (And firstly... etc.): The author's purpose with that is to divide the universal into essential, accidental, and intermediate. And this is taken from his statement by way of implication, since he restricted the first with 'inclusion in the essence' and the second with 'exit from it'. So it is known from this that the species is an intermediate; because it is neither included in the essence nor outside it, rather it is the essence itself. And this is one of three conventions that became famous among many conventions in that. The second: that the essential is what is included in the essence and the accidental is what is not like that; and according to this the species is accidental. The third: that the accidental is what exits from the essence and the essential is what is not like that; and according to this the species is essential. And clarification of that: the universal is either included in the essence, i.e. it is a part of it, and that is genus and differentia; or outside it, i.e. it is not a part of it nor its essence, and that is property and common accident; or neither included nor outside, i.e. it is the complete essence, and that is the species. So the essence (al-dhat) meaning the quiddity (al-mahiyya) like 'rational animal' in relation to 'man', and what is included in it like 'animal' and 'rational', and what is outside it like 'laughing' and 'walking', and what is neither included nor outside like 'man'. And it is not hidden from you the application of the mentioned disagreement to what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn line about the universal. The author (al-Bajuri) explains that the matn's phrase 'firstly for the essential if it is included' implies a division of the universal into three: essential (included in the essence), accidental (outside the essence), and intermediate (which is the species itself). He then notes three famous conventions among logicians: (1) The species is intermediate, as per the matn. (2) Another convention defines essential as what is included, accidental as what is not included, making the species accidental. (3) A third convention defines accidental as what is outside, essential as what is not outside, making the species essential. He clarifies by listing the five universals: genus and differentia are included in the essence (they are parts), property and common accident are outside, and the species is the complete essence. He gives examples: 'rational animal' is the essence of 'man'; 'animal' and 'rational' are parts; 'laughing' and 'walking' are outside; 'man' itself is the species. The disagreement about the species depends on which convention one adopts.

Key Terms
الذاتي
العرضي
النوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the second convention mentioned in the passage, the species is considered:
A) Essential (dhati)
B) Accidental (aradi)
C) Intermediate (wasit)
D) Both essential and accidental

Key Takeaway
The species is the complete essence, but its classification as essential, accidental, or intermediate depends on the convention adopted regarding the definitions of 'essential' and 'accidental'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'wudu' as 'washing the face and hands up to the elbows, wiping the head, and washing the feet up to the ankles with the intention of worship'. Identify its genus and differentia, then classify the species 'wudu' under each of the three conventions.
?
Find a definition from Islamic theology (e.g., 'iman is belief in the heart, speech on the tongue, and action of the limbs') and determine whether the species (iman) is considered essential, accidental, or intermediate under the conventions discussed in this lesson.

The Five Universals
beginner
5 min
Classifying the Five Universals: Essential vs Accidental
Author defines essential and accidental and classifies the five universals based on inclusion in the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any universal as essential (dhātī) or accidental (ʿaraḍī) based on its relation to the quiddity, and identify which of the five universals it belongs to.

Core Idea
The five universals are distinguished by whether they are inside, outside, or identical to the essence (quiddity).

How do logicians decide whether a predicate like 'animal' or 'laughing' is part of what something really is? This passage from al-Bajūrī's commentary on the Sullam al-Murawnaq gives the key: the essential is what is included in the essence (quiddity), and the accidental is what exits from it. We will learn to apply this division to the five universals: genus, differentia, species, proper attribute, and common accident.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definitions
Essential (al-dhātī) is what does not depart from the essence, meaning it is part of the quiddity. Accidental (al-ʿaraḍī) is what exits from the essence, meaning it is not part of the quiddity.
The passage emphasizes that the species is essential because it is the complete essence itself.
2
Identify the three categories
The universal (al-kullī) can be: (1) included in the essence as a part (genus and differentia); (2) outside the essence (proper attribute and common accident); or (3) neither included nor outside, but the whole essence itself (species).
3
Apply examples
For the quiddity of 'man' as 'rational animal': genus 'animal' and differentia 'rational' are essential parts; proper attribute 'laughing' and common accident 'walking' are accidental; species 'man' is the complete essence.
4
Check the disagreement
The passage ends by noting that the disagreement about whether something is essential or accidental can be applied to this framework. This refers to differing views among logicians on specific cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ. (٣٠) وَأَوَّلاً لِلذَّاتِ إِنْ فِيهَا انْدَرَجُ فَانْسِبْهُ، أَوْ لِعَارِضِ إِذَا خَرَجْ. الباجوري: ثَالِثُهَا : أَنَّ العَرَضِيَ : مَا خَرَجَ عَنِ الذَّاتِ، وَالذَّاتِيَّ : مَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَالنَّوْعُ ذَاتِيُّ. وَتَوْضِيحُ ذَلِكَ : أَنَّ الكُلِّيَّ : - إِمَّا مُنْدَرجُ فِي الذَّاتِ ؛ بِأَنْ كَانَ جُزْءاً مِنْهَا ، وَهُوَ : الجِنْسُ ، وَالفَصْلُ . - وَإِمَّا خَارِجٌ عَنْهَا ؛ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ جُزْءاً مِنْهَا وَلَا عَيْنَهَا ، وَهُوَ : الخَاصَّةُ، وَالعَرَضُ العَامُ . - وَإِمَّا غَيْرُ مُنْدَرجِ وَغَيْرُ خَارج؛ بِأَنْ كَانَ تَمَامَ الذَّاتِ، وَهُوَ : النُّوْعُ . فَالذَّاتُ بِمَعْنَى المَاهِيَّةِ كَـ : «الحَيَوَانُ النَّاطِقُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الإِنْسَانُ ، وَالمُنْدَرجُ فِيهَا كَـ : «الحَيَوَانُ» وَكَ: «النَّاطِقُ، وَالخَارِجُ عَنْهَا كَ: الضَّاحِكُ وَكَ: «المَاشِي، وَغَيْرُ المُنْدَرجِ وَغَيْرُ الخَارج ـ «الإِنْسَانُ»، وَلَا يَخْفَى عَلَيْكَ تَنْزِيلُ الخِلَافِ المَذْكُورِ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ.
Section on investigations of words. (30) And 'firstly' for the essence if it is included therein, then ascribe it to it, or to an accident if it exits. Al-Bajuri: The third of them: that the accidental is what exits from the essence, and the essential is what is not like that. Upon this, the species is essential. And the clarification of that: that the universal is either included in the essence, in that it is a part of it, and it is the genus and the differentia; or outside it, in that it is not a part of it nor its very self, and it is the proper attribute and the common accident; or neither included nor outside, in that it is the complete essence, and it is the species. So the essence in the sense of quiddity is like 'rational animal' in relation to 'man'; that which is included in it is like 'animal' and like 'rational'; that which is outside it is like 'laughing' and like 'walking'; and that which is neither included nor outside is 'man'. And it is not hidden from you the application of the mentioned disagreement to what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory section. It begins by citing a line from the Sullam: 'And firstly, for the essence if it is included therein, then ascribe it, or to an accident if it exits.' The commentator, al-Bajuri, then explains the third meaning: the accidental is what departs from the essence, and the essential is what does not. Consequently, the species is essential. He then clarifies the division of universals: a universal is either (1) included in the essence as a part—this is the genus and differentia; (2) outside the essence, not a part nor the whole—this is the proper attribute and common accident; or (3) neither included nor outside, but the complete essence itself—this is the species. Examples are given: the essence (quiddity) of man is 'rational animal'; genus 'animal' and differentia 'rational' are parts included; proper attribute 'laughing' and common accident 'walking' are outside; and the species 'man' is the whole. The passage ends by noting that the disagreement (about whether something is essential or accidental) can be applied accordingly.

Key Takeaway
A universal is essential if it is part of the quiddity (genus, differentia) or is the whole quiddity (species); it is accidental if it is outside the quiddity (proper attribute, common accident).

How to Attribute Essential and Accidental Properties
Bajuri explains the derivation of 'dhati' and 'aradi' from the matn line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between essential (dhati) and accidental (aradi) attributes, identify the linguistic objections to their derivations, and explain the difference between al-arid and al-aradi.

Core Idea
Essential and accidental terms are technical; knowing their derivational objections deepens your grasp of logical terminology.

When logicians say 'dhati' and 'aradi', they are not following standard Arabic derivation. This passage from Bajuri reveals the logical-linguistic debate behind these terms, helping you see why precision in naming matters for the five universals.

Guided Path
1
Read the matn rule
The matn states: 'First for the essence if it is included within it, then attribute it; or for an accident when it exits.' Identify the two categories: essential attributes (part of the essence) and accidental attributes.
2
Understand 'dhat' and 'arid' in context
Bajuri glosses 'dhat' as quiddity (mahiyya) or referent. 'Arid' is the accident itself, like laughter. Recognize that 'dhati' is used for genus and differentia.
3
Examine the objection to 'dhati'
According to Arabic nisba rules, from 'dhat' (or 'dhawat') one would expect 'dhawawi', not 'dhati'. The objection is that the logician's term is irregular.
4
Understand the answer to the objection
Bajuri reports two answers: either it is a conventional naming, not a real attribution, or if it is a real attribution, it is irregular. This clarifies that logical terminology can deviate from strict grammar.
5
Distinguish 'arid' from 'aradi'
Arid is the accident itself (e.g., laughter), while aradi is the thing described by the accident (e.g., the laugher). This distinction is crucial for applying the five universals correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلاً لِلذَّاتِ إِنْ فِيهَا انْدَرَجُ فَانْسِبْهُ، أَوْ لِعَارِضِ إِذَا خَرَجْ. قَوْلُهُ : (لِلذَّاتِ) أَيْ : لِلمَاهِيَّةِ كَمَا هُوَ أَحَدُ إِطْلَاقَيْهَا ، وَثَانِيهُمَا: إِطْلَاقُهَا عَلَى المَاصَدَقِ . قَوْلُهُ : (إِنْ فِيهَا انْدَرَج) أَيْ : بِأَنْ كَانَ جُزْءاً مِنْهَا ، وَهُوَ الجِنْسُ وَالفَصْلُ كَمَا مَرَّ . قَوْلُهُ : (فَانْسِبْهُ) أَيْ: بِأَنْ تَقُولَ: «ذَاتِيُّ ، كَمَا هُوَ الشَّائِعُ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ . وَيُحِثَ فِيهِ : بِأَنَّ مُقْتَضَى قَوَاعِدِ النَّسَبِ أَنْ يُقَالَ: «ذَوَوِيُّ» ؛ لِأَنَّ أَصْلَ المَنْسُوبِ إِلَيْهِ ذَوَو» ، وَالنَّسَبُ يَرِدُّ الأَشْيَاءَ إِلَى أُصُولِهَا . وَأُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ نَسَباً حَقِيقَةٌ، بَلْ تَسْمِيةٌ اصْطِلَاحِيَّةٌ عَلَى صُورَةِ النَّسَبِ، وَعَلَى تَسْلِيمِ أَنَّهُ نَسَبٌ حَقِيقَةٌ، فَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْرِ قِيَاسِ . قَوْلُهُ : (أَوْ لِعَارِضِ) أَيْ : أَوِ انْسِبُهُ لِعَارِضِ بِأَنْ تَقُولَ : عَرَضَيٌّ ، كَمَا هُوَ الشَّائِعُ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ . وَيُحِثَ فِيهِ أَيْضاً : بِأَنَّهُ كَانَ مُقْتَضَى الظَّاهِرِ أَنْ يُقَالَ: «عَارِضِيُّ». وَيُجَابُ بِمَا تَقَدَّمَ آنفاً . وَالمُرَادُ بِـ العَارِضِ»: المَنْسُوبُ إِلَيْهِ الأَمْرُ الَّذِي يَعْرِضُ لِلشَّيْء كَ: «الضَّحِكِ»، وَبِـ«العَرَضِيّ : المَنْسُوبُ نَحْوُ : «الصَّاحِكِ ، فَالعَارِضُ غَيْرُ العَرَضِيِّ، كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى.
And first for the essence if it is included within it, then attribute it, or for an accident when it exits. His statement: 'for the essence' means for the quiddity as is one of its two usages, and the second of them is its usage upon the referent. His statement: 'if it is included within it' means that it is a part of it, and it is the genus and the differentia as has passed. His statement: 'then attribute it' means by saying 'essential', as is customary among the logicians. And there is an objection against it: that the requirement of the rules of attribution is that it be said 'dhawawi' because the origin of the thing attributed to is 'dhawat', and attribution returns things to their origins. And it is answered: that that is not a real attribution, but a conventional naming in the form of an attribution, and even if it is conceded that it is a real attribution, then it is irregular. His statement: 'or for an accident' means: or attribute it to an accident by saying 'accidental', as is customary among the logicians. And there is an objection against it also: that the apparent requirement would be to say 'aradiyy' (with a ya'). And it is answered with what preceded just now. And what is meant by 'al-arid' is that to which the thing that occurs to the thing is attributed, like 'laughter', and by 'al-aradi' is the attributed thing like 'the laugher', so 'al-arid' is other than 'al-aradi', as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn line that instructs how to attribute something: if it is a part of the essence (genus or differentia), call it 'dhati' (essential); if it is an accident occurring to it, call it 'aradi' (accidental). The commentator first explains the matn's terms: 'dhat' here means the quiddity (mahiyya) or its referent. Then he notes that the term 'dhati' is conventional among logicians, not derived by standard Arabic rules; he responds to an objection that the correct Arabic derived form would be 'dhawawi' (from 'dhawat'), but answers that it is a technical name, not a real attribution. Similarly for 'aradi', an objection that it should be 'aradiyy' is answered the same way. Finally, he distinguishes between 'al-arid' (the accident itself, like laughter) and 'al-aradi' (the thing described by the accident, like the laugher). This guards against confusing the accidental property with the thing that possesses it.

Key Terms
ذاتي
عارض
عرضي

D) al-mahiyya

Key Takeaway
The terms 'dhati' and 'aradi' are conventional names, not standard Arabic derivations, and careful distinction between the accident and its attributed subject is essential for logical precision.

The Five Universals and the Definition of Genus
Enumeration and definition of genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five universals and explain the definition of genus with its qualifying conditions.

Core Idea
The five universals are classified by their relation to quiddity: part, whole, or external.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational enumeration of the five universals (al-kulliyat al-khams) from the classical logic curriculum. The commentator Bajuri not only lists them but also provides the rationale for why they are exactly five: every universal is either a part of the quiddity, the whole quiddity, or external to it. We then focus on the definition of the first universal – genus (jins) – and unpack its precise conditions: it must be true in answer to 'what is it?' and applicable to many things that differ in reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five universals from the matn
Locate the list in the Arabic: جنس، فصل، عرض، نوع، خاص. Note that 'عرض' is general accident, 'خاص' is property.
2
Understand the division rationale
The commentator explains: a universal is either part of the quiddity (genus and differentia), the whole (species), or external (property and general accident). This gives exactly five.
3
Analyze the definition of genus
The text says: 'ما صدق في جواب ما هو؟ على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقيقة'. Break it down: 'ما صدق في جواب ما هو؟' = it is what is true in answer to 'what is it?' – this is the generic condition. 'على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقيقة' = of many differing in reality – this is the specific condition that distinguishes genus from species and differentia.
4
Apply the definition with the example
The example 'animal' is true in answer to 'what is it?' for man, horse, donkey. Check that these differ in reality (different species) and that 'animal' applies to each. This confirms it is a genus.
The example guards against confusing genus with differentia: a differentia (e.g., rational) is not true in answer to 'what is it?' for many differing in reality – it specifies the species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالكُلِّيَاتُ خَمْسَةٌ دُونَ انْتِقَاصُ جِنْسٌ وَفَصْلٌ، عَرَضُ، نَوْعٌ، وَخَاصُ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَالكُلِّيَاتُ) بِتَخْفِيفِ اليَاءِ لِلوَزْنِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : (خَمْسَةٌ دُونَ انْتِقَاصُ أَيْ : وَدُونَ زِيَادَةٍ ; فَفِي كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ اكْتِفَاهُ عَلَى حَدٌ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: سَرَابِيلَ تَقِيكُمُ الْحَرَّ [النحل: ۸۱] أَيْ: وَالبَرْدَ . وَوَجْهُ انْحِصَارِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ فِي الخَمْسَةِ : أَنَّ الكُلِّيَّ : إِمَّا جُزْءٌ مِنَ المَاهِيَّةِ ، وَهُوَ : الجِنْسُ ، وَالفَصْلُ . وَإِمَّا تَمَامُهَا، وَهُوَ : النَّوْعُ. وَإِمَّا خَارِجٌ عَنْهَا ، وَهُوَ : الخَاصَّةُ، وَالعَرَضُ العَامُ . قَوْلُهُ : (جِنْسٌ) هُوَ : مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ مُخْتَلِفَينِ بِالحَقِيقَةِ، كَالْحَيَوَانِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ ... إلخ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَصِحُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ ، فَإِذَا قِيْلَ : الإِنْسَانُ وَالفَرَسُ وَالحِمَارُ مَا هُوَ؟ صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: «حَيَوَانُ» ; أَي : المَذْكُورُ حَيَوانٌ.
And the universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, and property. His statement: 'the universals' with lightening of the ya' for the meter. And his statement: 'five without deficiency' means without addition; so in the author's speech there is an abbreviation like His statement Exalted: 'Garments to protect you from heat' [Quran 16:81] meaning 'and from cold'. And the reason for the enumeration of the universals in five is that the universal: either it is a part of the quiddity, and it is the genus and the differentia; or it is the whole of it, and it is the species; or it is external to it, and it is the property and the general accident. His statement: 'genus' is what is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many differing in reality, like 'animal', for it is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many... etc.; meaning that it is valid to predicate it of what was mentioned, so if it is said: 'What is man, horse, and donkey?' it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that of what was mentioned by saying 'animal', meaning the mentioned thing is an animal.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage begins with the matn line listing the five universals (al-kulliyat al-khams): genus, differentia, species, general accident, and property. The commentator first notes a metrical lightening of the ya' in 'kulliyat'. He explains that 'without deficiency' means without addition or subtraction, and he gives an example of ellipsis from the Quran (interpretation of 'heat' to also imply cold). Then he provides the rationale for the fivefold classification: a universal is either a part of the quiddity (genus or differentia), the complete quiddity (species), or external to it (property or general accident). He then defines genus: what is predicated in answer to 'what is it?' of many differing in reality (like 'animal' for man, horse, donkey). He expands on this, explaining that it means it is valid to predicate 'animal' in answer to 'what is it?' for those subjects. This guards against confusing genus with differentia or accident.

عرض

Key Takeaway
The five universals are derived from the possible relations of a universal to the quiddity: part (genus/differentia), whole (species), or external (property/accident).

The Five Universals

Defining Genus (Jins) in the Five Universals
Al-Bajuri defines genus as what answers 'what is it?' for multiple differing species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus in any definition and distinguish it from other universals by applying the criteria of answering 'what is it?' and covering multiple differing species.

Core Idea
Genus answers 'what is it?' for at least two species differing in essence.

In this passage, al-Bajuri unpacks the classical definition of genus (jins) from al-Sullam. Understanding what makes something a genus—and what it is not—is essential for building correct definitions in any Islamic science. We will walk through each part of the definition and see how it excludes common accidents, differentiae, properties, and definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The term being defined is 'jins' (genus). Locate the sentence that begins with 'Jinsun huwa' and note the full definition given.
2
Extract the defining components
The definition has four key parts: (1) 'ma' (universal), (2) 'fi jawab ma huwa' (answers 'what is it?'), (3) 'ala kathirin' (of many), (4) 'mukhtalifin bi al-haqiqah' (differing in reality). Understand that each part is necessary.
The word 'ma' here refers to the universal as a genus of all universals.
3
Check the number of species
The definition says 'many' (kathirin). Al-Bajuri explains that this means at least two species, not three as the plural normally implies. This prevents the absurd consequence that no genus could cover fewer than six species.
This is a technical concession (musamahah) by the authors.
4
See what is excluded
The phrase 'fi jawab ma huwa' excludes the common accident (al-'arad al-'amm), because it answers 'how is it?'. Adding the consideration of 'ma' also excludes the differentia (fasl) and property (khassah), which answer 'which thing?'. The phrase 'ala kathirin' excludes the definition (hadd), which answers 'what is it?' for only one species.
For example, 'healthy' is not a genus because it does not answer 'what is it?'. 'Rational animal' is not a genus because it applies only to man.
5
Apply the definition to examples
Test the definition: 'Animal' is a genus because it answers 'what is it?' for man, horse, donkey (multiple species differing in reality). 'Rational animal' is not a genus; it is a hadd (definition) for a single species.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (جِنْسٌ) هُوَ : مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ مُخْتَلِفَينِ بِالحَقِيقَةِ، كَ «الحَيَوَانُ»، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟» عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ ... إلخ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَصِحُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ ، فَإِذَا قِيْلَ : الإِنْسَانُ وَالفَرَسُ وَالحِمَارُ مَا هُوَ؟ صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: «حَيَوَانُ» ؛ أَي : المَذْكُورُ حَيَوانٌ.
وَمَا : وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ.
وَالمُرَادُ بِـ الكَثِيرِينَ» : مَا يَشْمَلُ اثْنَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ ، وَالتَّعْبِيرُ بِذَلِكَ إِنَّمَا هُوَ مِنْ مُسَامِحَاتِ المُصَنِّفِينَ الَّتِي مُقْتَضَاهَا غَيْرُ مُرَادٍ، فَانْدَفَعَ مَا قَدْ يُقَالُ: إِنَّ كَثِيرِينَ جَمْعُ: «كَثِيرٍ، وَأَقَلُّ الجَمْعِ اثْنَانِ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِالجَمْعِ مَا فَوْقَ الوَاحِدِ، وَأَقَلُّ الكَثْرَةِ ثَلَاثَةٌ ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَصْلُحَ لِأَنْ يَصْدُقَ عَلَى أَقَلِّ مِنْ سِتَّةِ أَنْوَاعِ، وَهُوَ بَاطِلٌ.
وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا : فِي جَوَابِ) بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الإِضَافَةِ لِـ «مَا » : العَرَضُ العَامُّ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَقَعُ فِي الجَوَابِ المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَإِنْ وَقَعَ فِي الجَوَابِ عَنِ السُّؤالِ بِـ كَيْفَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ : كَيْفَ زَيْدٌ؟»، فَيُقَالُ: «صَحِيحٌ مثلاً.
وَمَعَ النَّظَرِ لِلإِضَافَةِ لِـ «مَا ) : الفَصْلُ وَالخَاصَّةُ ؛ لأَنَّ كُلَّا مِنْهُمَا لَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابٍ «ما»، وَإِنَّمَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ؟»، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا يَأْتِي.
وَبِقَوْلِنَا : عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ» : الحَدُّ ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟» عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ، بَلْ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى وَاحِدٍ فَقَط ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ : الإِنْسَانُ مَا هُوَ؟»، فَيُقَالُ: «حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ».
His saying: (Jins) is: that which is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many differing in reality, like 'animal', for it is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many... etc., meaning: that it is correct to predicate it of what was mentioned. So if it is said: 'Man, horse, and donkey: what is it?' it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that according to what was mentioned in the question, by saying 'animal', i.e., the mentioned things are animals. And (ma) refers to the universal that encompasses all universals, so it is a genus. And by 'many' is meant that which includes two or more. The expression with that is from the concessions of the authors whose implication is not intended. Thus is repelled what might be said: that 'kathirin' is the plural of 'kathir', and the minimum of the plural is two, based on the view that the plural means more than one, and the minimum of multiplicity is three, so it would follow that it would not be true of less than six species, which is false. And by our saying 'in answer to' (fi jawab), disregarding the addition of 'ma', there exits the common accident, because it does not occur in the conventionally accepted answer among the logicians, even if it occurs in answer to the question with 'how?', such as if it is said 'How is Zayd?' and it is said 'healthy' for example. And with consideration of the addition of 'ma', there exits the differentia and the property, because neither of them occurs in answer to 'ma', but rather they occur in answer to 'which thing?', as is known from what follows. And by our saying 'of many' (ala kathirin), there exits the definition (hadd), for it is not true in answer to 'what is it?' of many, but is true in answer to 'what is it?' of only one, as if it is said: 'What is man?' and it is said: 'Rational animal'.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the definition of genus (jins) as given in the matn of al-Sullam. The author, al-Bajuri, explains each component of the definition. The definition states: Genus is that which is true in answer to the question 'what is it?' (ma huwa) regarding many individuals that differ in reality (i.e., belong to different species). The example given is 'animal': when asked 'What is man?', 'What is horse?', 'What is donkey?', the answer 'animal' applies to all. The commentary then clarifies the term 'ma' (what) in the definition—it refers to the universal that encompasses all universals, so 'ma' itself is a genus (of all universals). Next, the commentary addresses the term 'kathirin' (many). The author notes that 'kathirin' is the plural of 'kathir', and while the minimum of the plural is two, the intended meaning here is strictly 'two or more', not the conventional linguistic minimum of three. This avoids the absurd consequence that genus would require at least six species (since the minimum of 'kathirin' would be three, and multiplied by two species each gives six). Then the commentary explains what is excluded by each part of the definition. The phrase 'in answer to' (fi jawab) without considering the addition of 'ma' excludes the common accident ('arad 'amm), because the common accident does not answer 'what is it?' but rather 'how is it?' (e.g., 'How is Zayd? Healthy'). When considering the addition of 'ma' (i.e., the question 'ma huwa?' specifically), the differentia (fasl) and property (khass) are also excluded, because they answer 'which thing?' (ayyu shay') not 'what is it?'. Finally, the phrase 'of many' excludes the definition (hadd), because the definition (e.g., 'rational animal') answers 'what is it?' for only one species (man), not for many.

Key Takeaway
Genus is a universal that answers 'what is it?' for at least two species differing in essence, distinguishing it from definition, differentia, property, and common accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether 'rational animal' (al-insan al-natiq) can be a genus according to the criteria in this lesson. Explain why or why not, referencing the requirement of covering multiple differing species.
?
The common accident 'laughter' answers 'how is it?' not 'what is it?'. Using the definition of genus, explain why 'laughter' is not a genus and what universal category it belongs to.

The Five Universals
intermediate
8 min
The Five Universals: Genus, Species, Differentia, Property, General Accident
Al-Bajuri and al-Anbabi define each of the five universals with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the five universals by the type of question it answers ('what is it?' or 'which thing?') and distinguish them from a complete definition (hadd).

Core Idea
Five universals are distinguished by which question they answer and whether they apply to many or one.

Logic provides five universal predicable categories that classify how terms can be predicated of many. This lesson walks through each universal as defined by classical logicians, focusing on the precise interrogative each one answers. By understanding these distinctions, you will be able to analyze any definition in Islamic sciences, from fiqh to kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the interrogative framework
Notice that the text uses 'ma' (what is it?) and 'ayyu shay'in' (which thing?) to classify universals. Observe that 'ma' itself is a genus encompassing all universals, while 'ayyu' divides essence from accident.
2
Classify each universal by question and scope
Genus and species answer 'what is it?' – genus applies to many differing in reality, species to many agreeing in reality. Differentia and property answer 'which thing?' – differentia about essence, property about accident. General accident does not answer either conventionally.
3
Exclude the complete definition (hadd)
The hadd (e.g., 'rational animal' for man) answers 'what is it?' for only one species, not many. Thus it is not a universal predicable.
4
Apply to an Islamic science example
Take the definition of wudu in fiqh: 'Wudu is washing certain limbs in a specific manner.' The genus could be 'washing', the species is 'wudu', the differentia is 'the specific manner and intention'. Identify which universal each part corresponds to.

وَالْكُلِّيَاتُ خَمْسَةٌ دُونَ انْتِقَاصٍ: جِنْسٌ، وَفَصْلٌ، عَرَضٌ، نَوْعٌ، وَخَاصٌ. الباجوري: وَمَا : وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ. وَالمُرَادُ بِـ المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَإِنْ وَقَعَ فِي الجَوَابِ عَنِ السُّؤَالِ بِـ كَيْفَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ : كَيْفَ زَيْدٌ؟، فَيُقَالُ: صَحِيحٌ مَثَلاً. وَمَعَ النَّظَرِ لِلإِضَافَةِ لِـ مَا : الفَصْلُ وَالخَاصَّةُ ؛ لأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا لَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا، وَإِنَّمَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ؟، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا يَأْتِي. وَبِقَوْلِنَا : عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ : الحَدُّ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ، بَلْ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى وَاحِدٍ فَقَط؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: الإِنْسَانُ مَا هُوَ؟، فَيُقَالَ: حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ. الأنبابي: قوله : (وَالمُرَادُ بِـ الكَثِيرِينَ ... إلخ) وغلب فيه أيضاً العاقل على غيره حتّى يصح الجمع بالياء. قوله : ( في الجَوَابِ المُصْطَلَحِ) وهو الجواب عنِ السُّؤال بـ ما أو أيُّ. ثم الباجوري: وَبِقَوْلِنَا : مُخْتَلِفِينَ بِالحَقِيقَةِ: النَّوْعُ، فَإِنَّهُ وَإِنْ صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ، لَكِنْ مُتَّفِقَيْنِ بِالحَقِيقَةِ كَمَا سَيَأْتِي. وَأَمَّا الجُزْئِيُّ فَلَا حَاجَةَ لِإِخْرَاجِهِ؛ لِمَا عَلِمْتَ مِنْ أَنَّ مَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى كُلِّيِّ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَنَّ الكَلَامَ لَيْسَ إِلَّا فِي الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَافْهَمْ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَفَصْلٌ هُوَ : مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟؛ كَ: النَّاطِقِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ، فَإِذَا قِيلَ: مُمَيِّرُ الإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟؛ أَيْ: حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مُنْدَرِجًا فِي ذَاتِهِ، صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: نَاطِقٌ، وَهَذَا مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى القَوْلِ بِأَنَّ النَّاطِقَ لَا يُقَالُ إِلَّا عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ، وَأَمَّا عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ: مِنْ أَنَّهُ يُقَالُ عَلَى المَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ، فَلَيْسَ النَّاطِقُ فَصْلاً لِلإِنْسَانِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلمَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ. وَمَا : وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ. وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا : فِي جَوَابِ : - بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الإِضَافَةِ لِـ أَيُّ : العَرَضُ العَامُّ . - وَمَعَ النَّظَرِ لَهَا : الجِنْسُ وَالنَّوْعُ ؛ لأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا لَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ، وَإِنَّمَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا. وَبِقَوْلِنَا : فِي ذَاتِهِ : الخَاصَّةُ، فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟، بَلْ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ؟.
The universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, and property. Al-Bajuri: 'What' (maa) is predicated on the universal that includes all universals, so it is a genus. What is meant by 'many' is that which includes two or more, and the expression here is from the looseness of the authors whose implication is not intended, thus it repels what might be said: that 'many' is the plural of 'much', and the least of the plural is two, based on that the intended meaning of plural is what is above one, and the least of multiplicity is three, so it would be necessary that it not be valid to be true of less than six species, which is false. And by our saying 'in answer' — disregarding the relation to 'what' — the general accident is excluded because it does not fall in the conventional answer according to the logicians, even if it falls in the answer to the question with 'how' such as if it is said: 'How is Zayd?' and it is said: 'Healthy' for example. And with consideration of the relation to 'what', the differentia and property are excluded because neither of them falls in the answer to 'what', but rather they fall in the answer to 'which thing?' as will be known from what follows. And by our saying 'upon many', the limit (hadd) is excluded, for it is not true in answer to 'what is it?' of many, but rather it is true in answer to 'what is it?' of one only, as if it is said: 'What is man?' and it is said: 'A rational animal'. Al-Anbabi: His statement (the intended meaning of 'many'... etc.) and it also overcomes the rational over other than it so that the plural with the ya' is valid. His statement (the conventional answer) is the answer to the question with 'what' or 'which'. Then Al-Bajuri: And by our saying 'differing in reality' the species is excluded, for it, even if it is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many, but they are agreeing in reality as will come. And as for the particular, there is no need for its exclusion because of what you know that 'what' is predicated on a universal by virtue of the discourse being only about universals, so understand. His statement: (And a differentia is what is true in answer to 'which thing is it in its essence?' such as 'rational', for it is true in that answer. So if it is said: 'The differentiator of man: which thing is it in its essence?' i.e., in the state of being comprehended in his essence, it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that upon what was mentioned in the question by saying: 'Rational'. And this is based on the statement that 'rational' is not said except of man. And as for what some said, that it is said of angels and jinn, then 'rational' is not a differentia for man with respect to angels and jinn. And 'what' is predicated on the universal that includes all universals, so it is a genus. And by our saying 'in answer': — disregarding the relation to 'which', the general accident is excluded. — And with consideration of it, genus and species are excluded, because neither of them falls in the answer to 'which', but rather they fall in the answer to 'what'. And by our saying 'in its essence', the property is excluded, for it is not true in answer to 'which thing is it in its essence?', but rather in answer to 'which thing is it in its accident?'.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defining the five universals (al-kulliyat al-khams). The matn states: 'The universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, property.' Al-Bajuri begins by noting that the interrogative word 'ma' (what) is itself a universal that includes all universals, so it is a genus. He then clarifies the meaning of 'many' (kathirin) in the definition of genus: it means two or more, not strictly three, because the term 'kathirin' is used loosely. This resolves an objection that the plural of 'much' requires at least three, which would make the definition false for two individuals. Next, by the phrase 'in answer' with disregard to the relation to 'ma', the general accident is excluded—it does not answer 'what is it?' in the technical sense, though it may answer 'how?' (like saying 'Zayd is healthy'). When considering the relation to 'ma', the differentia and property are excluded because they answer 'which thing?' (ayyu shay'in), not 'what?'. By 'upon many', the limit (hadd) is excluded because it answers 'what is it?' for only one thing, e.g., 'man is a rational animal'. Al-Anbabi adds that in 'many', the rational beings are emphasized for plural validity. Then Al-Bajuri defines species: it answers 'what is it?' for many that agree in reality. The particular (juz'i) is not excluded because discourse is only about universals. The differentia is defined as what answers 'which thing is it in its essence?', like 'rational' for man, noting the condition that 'rational' applies only to humans, not to angels or jinn. Finally, the property is what answers 'which thing is it in its accident?', not in its essence. Thus, each universal is distinguished by the type of question it answers.

Key Terms
جنس
نوع
فصل
خاصة
عرض عام
حد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Genus (jins)
B) Species (naw')
C) Differentia (fasl)

Key Takeaway
The five universals are classified by the type of interrogative they answer and whether they apply to many or one, forming the foundation for logical definition in Islamic sciences.

The Differentia (Fasl): Definition and Distinction
Bajuri defines the differentia and explains what is excluded from its definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct definition of the differentia (fasl) and distinguish it from common accident, genus, species, and property based on the criteria of 'in answer to what is it in its essence?'.

Core Idea
The differentia answers 'what is it in its essence?' while property answers 'what is it in its accident?'.

In the five universals, the differentia (fasl) is the attribute that distinguishes a species within its genus. It is not enough to say something is distinctive; it must answer a specific question about essence. Bajuri's commentary clarifies this by explaining what is included and excluded in the definition, using the example of 'rational' for man. Let's dissect this definition step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the definiens
The definiendum is 'fasl' (differentia). The definiens is 'what is true in answer to: what is it in its essence?'. Locate this in the Arabic: 'فَصْلٌ هُوَ: «مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟»'.
The phrase 'ma sadaqa' is the definiens and it itself is a universal genus.
2
Understand the role of 'ma'
Bajuri explains that 'ma' in the definition applies to a universal that encompasses all universals, i.e., it is a genus. This ensures the definition covers all differentiae.
3
Examine the question 'what is it in its essence?'
The differentia must be true in answer to 'ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatihi?' (what is it in its essence?). This question targets the essential attribute. Contrast with 'mā huwa?' (what is it?) which is answered by genus or species.
The word 'ayyu' specifies the type of question.
4
Analyze the example 'rational' for man
The example is 'natiq' (rational) for man. When asked 'What is the distinguisher of man in his essence?', the answer 'natiq' fits. But note: if one holds that 'natiq' also applies to angels and jinn, it would not be a differentia for man relative to them.
This highlights that a differentia must be coextensive with the species.
5
Determine what is excluded
By 'in answer to' (without considering relation to 'ayyu'): common accident is excluded. Considering 'ayyu': genus and species are excluded (they answer 'mā' not 'ayyu'). By 'in its essence': property (khassah) is excluded (it answers 'what is it in its accident?').
Each exclusion sharpens the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الجُزْئِيُّ فَلَا حَاجَةَ لِإِخْرَاجِهِ؛ لِمَا عَلِمْتَ مِنْ أَنَّ مَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى كُلِّيٍّ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَنَّ الكَلَامَ لَيْسَ إِلَّا فِي الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَافْهَمْ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَفَصْلٌ هُوَ: «مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟»؛ كَ: «النَّاطِقِ»، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ، فَإِذَا قِيلَ: «مُمَيِّزُ الإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟»؛ أَيْ: حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مُنْدَرِجًا فِي ذَاتِهِ، صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: «نَاطِقٌ»، وَهَذَا مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى القَوْلِ بِأَنَّ النَّاطِقَ لَا يُقَالُ إِلَّا عَلَى الإِنْسَانِ، وَأَمَّا عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ: مِنْ أَنَّهُ يُقَالُ عَلَى المَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ، فَلَيْسَ النَّاطِقُ فَصْلًا لِلإِنْسَانِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلمَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ. وَمَا وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ، فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ. وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا: فِي جَوَابِ: - بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الإِضَافَةِ لِـ«أَيُّ»: العَرَضُ العَامُّ. - وَمَعَ النَّظَرِ لَهَا: الجِنْسُ وَالنَّوْعُ؛ لِأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا لَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ «أَيُّ»، وَإِنَّمَا يَقَعُ فِي جَوَابِ «مَا». وَبِقَوْلِنَا: «فِي ذَاتِهِ»: الخَاصَّةُ، فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟، بَلْ فِي جَوَابِ «أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ؟».
As for the particular, there is no need to exclude it, because you know that 'ma' applies to a universal, considering that the discussion is only about universals, so understand. His statement: (And the differentia is: 'what is true in answer to: what is it in its essence?'; like 'rational', for it is true in answer to that. So if it is said: 'The distinguisher of man, what is it in its essence?', i.e., while it is included in his essence, it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that upon what was mentioned in the question, by saying 'rational'. And this is based on the position that 'rational' is said only of man. As for the position of some who say it is said of angels and jinn, then 'rational' is not a differentia for man in relation to angels and jinn. And 'ma' applies to the universal that encompasses all universals, so it is a genus. And what is excluded by our statement 'in answer to': - disregarding the relation to 'ayyu': the common accident. - With regard to it: genus and species, because each of them does not occur in answer to 'ayyu', but rather occurs in answer to 'ma'. And by our statement 'in its essence': the property, for it is not true in answer to 'what is it in its essence?', but rather in answer to 'what is it in its accident?')
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary from Bajuri on the concept of the differentia (fasl) within the five universals. The author first clarifies why the particular does not need to be excluded from the definition of the differentia, since the discussion is confined to universals. Then he presents the definition: the differentia is that which is true in answer to 'what is it in its essence?' (ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatihi?). The example given is 'rational' (al-natiq) for man. He explains that when asked 'what is the distinguisher of man in his essence?', the answer 'rational' fits. However, this is based on the view that 'rational' applies only to man; if one holds that it applies to angels and jinn as well, then 'rational' is not a differentia of man relative to them. The author also notes that the word 'ma' in the definition is a genus covering all universals. Then he explicates what falls outside the definition: by 'in answer to'—without considering the relation to 'ayyu'—the common accident is excluded; with consideration to 'ayyu', genus and species are excluded because they answer 'ma' not 'ayyu'. By 'in its essence', the property (khassah) is excluded because it answers 'what is it in its accident?' not 'what is it in its essence?'.

Key Terms
فَصْل (fasl)
عَرَضٌ عَامٌّ ('arad 'amm)
خَاصَّة (khassah)

Two Types of Differentia: Near and Far
Bajuri divides differentia into near and far.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between near differentia (fasl qarib) and far differentia (fasl ba'id) using the examples of 'rational' and 'sentient' for man.

Core Idea
A differentia's nearness or farness depends on the genus level it distinguishes from.

In defining a species, we often use a differentia to set it apart. But differentia can be 'near' or 'far' depending on how close the shared genus is. This lesson clarifies the two types with concrete examples from the logic of essences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Find the terms 'fasl qarib' and 'fasl ba'id' in the text.
2
Examine the near differentia example
Note that 'rational' distinguishes man from other animals; the near genus is 'animal'.
3
Examine the far differentia example
Note that 'sentient' distinguishes man from all bodies; the far genus is 'body'.
4
Analyze the relationship
The difference is which level of genus is being used for distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الفَصْلَ نَوْعَانِ: قَرِيبٌ، وَبَعِيدٌ. (١) - فَالأَوَّلُ: مَا يُمَيِّرُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ القَرِيبِ، كَـ«النَّاطِقِ»، فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُ الإِنْسَانَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ القَرِيبِ وَهُوَ الحَيَوَانُ مِنَ الفَرَسِ، وَالحِمَارِ، وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. (٢) - وَالثَّانِي: مَا يُمَيِّرُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ البَعِيدِ، كَـ«الحَسَّاسِ» بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلإِنْسَانِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُهُ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ البَعِيدِ كَالجِسْمِ مِنَ الحَجَرِ، وَالشَّجَرِ، وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: يَلْزَمُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ كَوْنُ الجِنْسِ غَيْرِ العَالِي فَصْلًا؛ لِأَنَّهُ يُمَيِّرُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ البَعِيدِ، كَـ«الحَيَوَانِ» بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلإِنْسَانِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُهُ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي الجِنْسِ البَعِيدِ كَالجِسْمِ مِنَ الحَجَرِ، وَالشَّجَرِ، وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. أُجِيبَ: بِأَنَّ الحَيَوَانَ مَثَلًا إِذَا وَقَعَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ؟، كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ: «مُمَيِّزُ الإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟»، فَقُلْتَ: «حَيَوَانٌ»، كَانَ فَصْلًا.
And know that the differentia is of two types: near and far. (1) The first: what distinguishes a thing from what shares its near genus, like 'rational', for it distinguishes man from what shares its near genus, which is animal, such as horse, donkey, and the like. (2) The second: what distinguishes a thing from what shares its far genus, like 'sentient' in relation to man, for it distinguishes him from what shares his far genus, such as body from stone, tree, and the like. If it is said: It follows from that that the genus (that is not the highest) is a differentia, because it distinguishes a thing from what shares its far genus, like 'animal' in relation to man, for it distinguishes him from what shares the far genus, such as body from stone, tree, and the like. The answer is: That animal, for instance, if it occurs in answer to 'what is it?', as when it is said: 'The distinguisher of man, what is it in its essence?', and you say 'animal', it would be a differentia.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage classifies the differentia into two types and then addresses an objection. The author defines the near differentia (fasl qarib) as that which distinguishes a thing from what shares its immediate genus (e.g., 'rational' distinguishes man from other animals). The far differentia (fasl ba'id) distinguishes from what shares a more remote genus (e.g., 'sentient' distinguishes man from inanimate bodies). An objection is then raised: if a far differentia distinguishes from a far genus, then a genus itself (like 'animal') could be considered a differentia because it also distinguishes man from non-animal bodies. The author responds by specifying that a genus becomes a differentia when it is used in answer to 'what is it in its essence?' (ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatihi?), i.e., when it is taken as a distinguishing characteristic. Thus, the same term can serve as genus or differentia depending on the context of the question.

Key Terms
فصل قريب
فصل بعيد
جنس غير عال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Rational' for man.
B) 'Animal' for man.
C) 'Sentient' for man.
D) 'Body' for man.

Key Takeaway
Differentia are classified as near or far based on the proximity of the genus from which they distinguish, with 'rational' as near and 'sentient' as far for man.

When Does a Genus Become a Differentia?
Bajuri responds to an objection about genus being a differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an intermediate genus (jins ghayr 'ali) can function as a differentia when used in answer to an essential question about a higher genus.

Core Idea
A genus can be a differentia when it answers 'what is it in its essence?' relative to a higher genus.

The passage raises a clever objection: if a far differentia distinguishes from a far genus, then a genus like 'animal' should also be a differentia. Bajuri's answer reveals that roles depend on the question being asked, not on fixed properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector says that a genus (like 'animal') distinguishes man from non-animal bodies, so it should be a differentia.
2
Understand the reasoning
The objector equates the function of a far differentia with that of a genus.
3
Examine the answer
The author says a genus becomes a differentia when it appears in answer to 'what is it in its essence?' (ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatihi?).
4
Apply the example
If someone asks about the distinguisher of man in its essence, answering 'animal' makes it a differentia.
5
Generalize the principle
The same term can serve different logical roles depending on context.

Source Text

And know that the differentia is of two types: near and far. (1) The first: what distinguishes a thing from what shares its near genus, like 'rational', for it distinguishes man from what shares its near genus, which is animal, such as horse, donkey, and the like. (2) The second: what distinguishes a thing from what shares its far genus, like 'sentient' in relation to man, for it distinguishes him from what shares his far genus, such as body from stone, tree, and the like. The author defines the near differentia (fasl qarib) as that which distinguishes a thing from what shares its immediate genus (e.g., 'rational' distinguishes man from other animals). Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does an intermediate genus (jins ghayr 'ali) act as a differentia?
A) Always, because it distinguishes from a far genus.
B) Never, because genus and differentia are mutually exclusive.
C) When it is used in answer to 'what is it in its essence?' (ayyu shay'in huwa fi dhatihi?).
D) Only when it is a highest genus (jins 'ali).

Key Takeaway
A genus becomes a differentia when it answers the question 'what is it in its essence?' relative to a higher genus, demonstrating that logical roles are context-dependent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the term 'prophet' (nabi). Could 'human' be a genus or a differentia for 'prophet'? Explain using the lesson's principle by answering 'what is the prophet in his essence?'.
