Refining the Definition of Differentia: From Genus to Existence
Anbab clarifies that later logicians added 'or in existence' to the definition of differentia to cover cases lacking a genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key difference between early and later scholars' definitions of differentia and explain why 'or in existence' was added.

Core Idea
The differentia does not always require a genus—later logicians added 'or in existence' to cover unique essences like God.

In this passage, the super-commentator Anbab, citing Sabban, reveals a crucial historical development in the definition of differentia. Early logicians assumed every differentia belongs to a genus, but later scholars recognized that some quiddities—like the Necessary Existent—have no genus. To accommodate this, they added the phrase 'or in existence' to the definition. This refinement safeguards the logical tool from being too narrow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the early view
Early logicians (mutaqaddimun) held that every quiddity (mahiyyah) with a differentia must have a genus. This is the basis of the standard definition that restricts 'differentia' to distinguishing within a genus.
This view is implicit in the wording 'in its near genus'.
2
Recognize the problem
Some quiddities, such as the Necessary Existent (God) or perhaps prime matter, have no genus at all. The early definition would exclude such entities from having a differentia, which is problematic because they still need to be distinguished from others.
The Necessary Existent is a standard example from kalam.
3
Find the later solution
Later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) added the phrase 'or in existence' (aw fi al-wujud) to the definition. The revised definition: the differentia distinguishes the thing in its essence from what shares it in genus OR in existence.
This allows a differentia to work even without a common genus, by using existence as the broader category.
4
Apply the refined definition
Under the new definition, a near differentia distinguishes from everything that shares existence (i.e., all other existing things), while a far differentia distinguishes only from some existents. Test with the Necessary Existent: its differentia 'necessary' distinguishes it from all contingent existents.
This preserves the logical function of differentia across all quiddities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فِي جِنْسِهِ القَرِيبِ ويلزم منه تمييزه عمَّا يشاركه في البعيد، بخلاف الفصل البعيد، فإنه لا يلزم من تمييزه الشَّيء عما يشاركه في البعيد تمييزه له عما يشاركه في القريب، والاقتصار على ذكر الجنس في النوعين مبني على أن كل ماهية لها فصل لا بد وأن يكون لها جنس، وهو مذهب المتقدمين. وذهب المتأخّرون إلى عدم لزوم ذلك، فزادوا في تعريف الفصل: أو في الوجود، فقالوا في تعريفه: ما يميز الشَّيء في ذاته عما يشاركه في الجنس، أو في الوجود، فإن كان هذا الفصل مميزًا للماهية عن جميع ما يشاركها في الوجود فهو قريب، وإن ميزها عن بعض ما يشاركها فيه فهو بعيد. اهـ «صبان».
His statement: '(in its near genus) and it follows from that its distinguishing it from what shares it in the far genus, contrary to the far differentia, for its distinguishing the thing from what shares it in the far genus does not necessitate its distinguishing it from what shares it in the near genus. And restricting the mention of genus in the two types is based on the fact that every quiddity that has a differentia must necessarily have a genus, and this is the doctrine of the early scholars. The later scholars held that this is not necessary, so they added to the definition of differentia: 'or in existence', and they said in its definition: what distinguishes the thing in its essence from what shares it in genus, or in existence. If this differentia distinguishes the quiddity from everything that shares it in existence, it is near; and if it distinguishes it from some of what shares it in existence, it is far.') End quote from Sabban.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the super-commentator Anbab, who draws on Sabban, regarding the definition of differentia. He begins by explaining a point from the earlier text: when the text mentions 'in its near genus' for the near differentia, it implies that the near differentia also distinguishes from the far genus, unlike the far differentia which does not necessarily distinguish from the near genus. Then he notes that the earlier definition presupposes that every quiddity (mahiyyah) that has a differentia must have a genus—this is the view of the early scholars (mutaqaddimin). The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) rejected this necessity, arguing that some quiddities may lack a genus (e.g., God or primal matter). Therefore, they modified the definition of differentia by adding 'or in existence' (aw fi al-wujud). The revised definition: the differentia distinguishes the thing in its essence from what shares it in genus or in existence. Under this, the near differentia distinguishes from everything that shares existence, and the far differentia distinguishes from only a portion.

Key Terms

الوُجُود
مُتَقَدِّمُونَ
مُتَأَخِّرُونَ

D) 'Or in property'.

Key Takeaway
The differentia can function without a genus by using existence as the broader category—a key refinement by later logicians.

Near and Far Differentia in the Five Universals
Author enumerates the five universals and defines near and far differentia with an objection-answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between near and far differentia and explain how the same term can function as a differentia or a genus depending on the context of the question.

Core Idea
Differentia is context-dependent: it can be a genus when answering 'what is it?' for multiple species.

The five universals are the building blocks of definition. Among them, differentia (fasl) is particularly subtle because whether a term counts as a differentia or a genus depends on the kind of question it answers. The author gives a concrete example: 'animal' can be a differentia for man if we ask about man's essence, but a genus if we ask about man and horse together. Let's see how this works.

Guided Path
1
List the five universals
Find the enumeration in the passage: genus, differentia, accident, species, and property. Note that the particular is excluded. Write them down.
2
Identify the two types of differentia
The passage divides differentia into near (qarib) and far (ba'id). Near differentia distinguishes a thing from what shares its immediate genus. Far differentia distinguishes from what shares a broader (far) genus.
3
Examine the examples
For near: 'rational' distinguishes man from horse and donkey, all within the immediate genus 'animal'. For far: 'sentient' distinguishes man from stone and tree, which are outside the immediate genus but within the far genus 'body'.
4
Analyze the objection and answer
The objector says: if 'animal' distinguishes man from stone, it should be a differentia. The author answers: it depends on the question. When asked 'what thing is it?' about man's essence, 'animal' is a differentia. When asked 'what is it?' about man and horse together, 'animal' is a genus.
This shows the same term can play different roles based on the intention.
5
Test the principle
Apply the same reasoning to another term like 'body' for man. If asked about man's essence, 'body' could serve as a far differentia; if asked about man and tree, it is a genus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْكُلِّيَاتُ خَمْسَةٌ دُونَ انْتِقَاصٍ: جِنْسٌ، وَفَصْلٌ، عَرَضٌ، نَوْعٌ، وَخَاصٌ. وَأَمَّا الْجُزْئِيُّ فَلَا حَاجَةَ لِإِخْرَاجِهِ لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْفَصْلَ نَوْعَانِ: قَرِيبٌ وَبَعِيدٌ. فَالْأَوَّلُ: مَا يُمَيِّزُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ الْقَرِيبِ، كَالنَّاطِقِ فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُ الْإِنْسَانَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ الْقَرِيبِ وَهُوَ الْحَيَوَانُ مِنَ الْفَرَسِ وَالْحِمَارِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. وَالثَّانِي: مَا يُمَيِّزُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ الْبَعِيدِ، كَالْحَسَّاسِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُهُ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ الْبَعِيدِ كَالْجِسْمِ مِنَ الْحَجَرِ وَالشَّجَرِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: يَلْزَمُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ كَوْنُ الْجِنْسِ غَيْرِ الْعَالِي فَصْلًا لِأَنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُ الشَّيْءَ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي جِنْسِهِ الْبَعِيدِ كَالْحَيَوَانِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ يُمَيِّزُهُ عَمَّا يُشَارِكُهُ فِي الْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيدِ كَالْجِسْمِ مِنَ الْحَجَرِ وَالشَّجَرِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ. أُجِيبَ: بِأَنَّ الْحَيَوَانَ مَثَلًا إِذَا وَقَعَ فِي جَوَابِ "أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ؟" كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ: مُمَيِّزُ الْإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟ فَقُلْتَ: حَيَوَانٌ، كَانَ فَصْلًا. وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي جَوَابِ "مَا هُوَ؟" كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ: الْإِنْسَانُ وَالْفَرَسُ مَا هُوَ؟ فَقُلْتَ: حَيَوَانٌ، كَانَ جِنْسًا. فَهُوَ فَصْلٌ بِاعْتِبَارٍ وَجِنْسٌ بِاعْتِبَارٍ آخَرَ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
And the universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, and property. As for the particular, there is no need to exclude it due to what has preceded. Know that differentia is of two types: near and far. The first: what distinguishes a thing from what shares with it in its near genus, like 'rational', for it distinguishes man from what shares with him in his near genus, which is animal, from horse, donkey, and the like. The second: what distinguishes a thing from what shares with it in its far genus, like 'sentient' in relation to man, for it distinguishes him from what shares with him in his far genus, like body from stone, tree, and the like. If it is said: it follows from that that the non-highest genus is a differentia, because it distinguishes a thing from what shares with it in its far genus, like 'animal' in relation to man, for it distinguishes him from what shares with him in the far genus, like body from stone, tree, and the like. It is answered: that animal, for example, if it occurs in the answer to 'what thing is it?' as when it is said: the distinguisher of man, what thing is it in its essence? and you said: animal, it is a differentia. And if it occurs in the answer to 'what is it?' as when it is said: man and horse, what are they? and you said: animal, it is a genus. So it is a differentia in one respect and a genus in another respect, so let it be contemplated.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage defines the five universals and focuses on differentia (fasl). The author first lists the five universals, noting that the particular (juz'i) is not included. Then he divides differentia into near and far. Near differentia (e.g., rational) distinguishes a species from other species within the same immediate genus (e.g., animal). Far differentia (e.g., sentient) distinguishes a species from things outside its immediate genus, such as inanimate bodies. An objection is raised: if a non-highest genus like animal distinguishes man from stone, why is it not a differentia? The answer distinguishes between two contexts: when the question is about the essence of a single thing ('what thing is it?'), 'animal' functions as a differentia; when the question asks about multiple species together ('what are they?'), 'animal' is a genus. Thus, the same term can be a differentia or genus depending on the question's intention.

Defining the Common Accident
Author defines common accident using genus and differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the common accident using its two definitional parts and distinguish it from property, species, genus, and differentia.

Core Idea
The common accident exits the essence and applies to many; property applies to only one species.

In the five universals, the common accident is the broadest non-essential attribute. The author gives a precise definition that excludes all other universals. Let's dissect it step by step so you can apply it in fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and its genus
The author defines 'al-'arad al-'amm'. The defining phrase begins with 'ma' (what), which functions as a genus indicator. What is the broader category? It is the universal that includes all universals – i.e., the concept of a universal itself.
2
Extract the differentia: 'exits the essence'
The first part of the definition: 'exits the essence' (kharaja 'an al-mahiyya). This excludes anything that is part of the essence: genus (jins), differentia (fasl), and species (naw'). These are internal to the mahiyya, not external.
The species is the complete essence; genus and differentia are its parts.
3
Extract the second differentia: 'and is true of it and others'
The second part: 'sadaqa 'alayha wa 'ala ghayriha' (is true of it and others). This excludes property (khassa), because property is true only of one species (e.g., laughing for man). Common accident must be true of multiple species.
4
Test with examples from the text
The author gives 'moving' as an example. 'Moving' exits the essence of man (man is defined as rational animal, not as moving) and is true of man, horse, bird, etc. So it is a common accident. 'Laughing' is true only of man, so it is property, not common accident.
Check each example: if it fails either condition, it is not a common accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (عَرَضُ) أَيْ: عَامٌ، وَهُوَ: مَا خَرَجَ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ وَصَدَقَ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا كَالْمُتَحَرِّكِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ خَرَجَ عَنْ مَاهِيَّتِهِ وَيَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: الْإِنْسَانُ مُتَحَرِّكٌ، وَالْفَرَسُ مُتَحَرِّكٌ. وَمَا: وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الْكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الْكُلِّيَّاتِ فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ. وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا: خَرَجَ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ الْجِنْسُ وَالْفَصْلُ وَالنَّوْعُ فَإِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ خَارِجَةً عَنْهَا بَلِ الْأُوَّلَانِ جُزْءَانِ مِنْهَا وَالثَّالِثُ تَمَامُهَا. وَبِقَوْلِنَا: وَصَدَقَ ... إلخ: الْخَاصَّةُ فَإِنَّهَا وَإِنْ خَرَجَتْ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ تَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا فَقَطْ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْعَرَضَ الْعَامَّ نَوْعَانِ: الْأَوَّلُ: لَازِمٌ كَالْمُتَنَفِّسِ بِالْقُوَّةِ. وَالثَّانِي: مُفَارِقٌ كَالْمُتَنَفِّسِ بِالْفِعْلِ.
His statement: 'accident' meaning common, and it is: what exits the essence and is true of it and of other than it, like 'moving' in relation to man, for it exits his essence and is true of him and of other than him, as when it is said: man is moving, and the horse is moving. And 'what' refers to the universal that includes all universals, so it is a genus. And by our statement: 'exits the essence' is excluded genus, differentia, and species, for they are not external to it, rather the first two are parts of it and the third is its complete [essence]. And by our statement: 'and is true... etc.' is excluded the property, for although it exits the essence, it is true only of it. And know that the common accident is of two types: the first: necessary, like 'breathing by potentiality'. And the second: separable, like 'breathing by actuality'.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines the common accident (al-'arad al-'amm). The author begins by stating that 'arad here means common, not special. He defines it as what is external to the essence (al-mahiyya) and is predicated of that essence and of other essences. Example: 'moving' is true of both man and horse. He then analyses the definition word by word. The word 'ma' (what) refers to the universal that covers all five universals, so it is a genus. The first part ('exits the essence') excludes the universals that are internal to the essence: genus (part), differentia (part), and species (the whole essence). The second part ('and is true of it and others') excludes property (khass), which is true only of one species. Finally, he divides common accident into two: necessary (lazim), which is inseparable like 'breathing by potentiality', and separable (mufariq), which can be absent like 'breathing by actuality'.

خاصة

Key Takeaway
A common accident is a non-essential attribute that applies to more than one species, defined by being external to the essence and multiply applicable.

Types of Common Accident: Necessary and Separable
Author divides common accident into necessary and separable with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between necessary and separable common accidents and classify examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
A necessary accident is always attached to the essence; a separable one can come and go.

After establishing what a common accident is, the author divides it into two types based on whether the attribute can be separated from the subject. This classification is essential in kalam and fiqh for understanding essential vs. accidental properties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
The author states: common accident is of two types – first: necessary (lazim), second: separable (mufariq). Understand the defining criterion: necessity means the attribute cannot be absent from the subject without destroying the subject's essence; separability means it can be present or absent.
2
Examine the examples from the text
For man: 'breathing by potentiality' (al-tanafus bil-quwwa) is necessary – man always has the potential to breathe. 'Breathing by actuality' (al-tanafus bil-fi'l) is separable – a man may be holding his breath or asleep. The same attribute can be necessary in one respect and separable in another.
Necessary does not mean always actual; it means the capacity is always present.
3
Test with other Islamic examples
Consider 'intoxication' for khamr: it is a necessary common accident? No, because wine always has the potential to intoxicate but not always actual; but for khamr, intoxication is a necessary accident (it cannot exist without the potential). For man, 'laughter' is a property, not common accident, but if we treat it as common accident (if it applied to hyenas), it would be separable rather than necessary.
Use the test: can the subject exist without the attribute? If yes, it is separable.
4
Apply to a fiqh ruling
In usul al-fiqh, the 'illah (effective cause) is often a necessary common accident of the ruling (hukm). For example, 'intoxication' is a necessary accident of wine and serves as the 'illah for prohibition. If the 'illah were separable, rulings could not be consistently attached.
This shows why distinguishing necessary from separable matters for legal analogy (qiyas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (عَرَضُ) أَيْ: عَامٌ، وَهُوَ: مَا خَرَجَ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ وَصَدَقَ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا كَالْمُتَحَرِّكِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ خَرَجَ عَنْ مَاهِيَّتِهِ وَيَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: الْإِنْسَانُ مُتَحَرِّكٌ، وَالْفَرَسُ مُتَحَرِّكٌ. وَمَا: وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الْكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الْكُلِّيَّاتِ فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ. وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا: خَرَجَ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ الْجِنْسُ وَالْفَصْلُ وَالنَّوْعُ فَإِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ خَارِجَةً عَنْهَا بَلِ الْأُوَّلَانِ جُزْءَانِ مِنْهَا وَالثَّالِثُ تَمَامُهَا. وَبِقَوْلِنَا: وَصَدَقَ ... إلخ: الْخَاصَّةُ فَإِنَّهَا وَإِنْ خَرَجَتْ عَنِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ تَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا فَقَطْ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْعَرَضَ الْعَامَّ نَوْعَانِ: الْأَوَّلُ: لَازِمٌ كَالْمُتَنَفِّسِ بِالْقُوَّةِ. وَالثَّانِي: مُفَارِقٌ كَالْمُتَنَفِّسِ بِالْفِعْلِ.
His statement: 'accident' meaning common, and it is: what exits the essence and is true of it and of other than it, like 'moving' in relation to man, for it exits his essence and is true of him and of other than him, as when it is said: man is moving, and the horse is moving. And 'what' refers to the universal that includes all universals, so it is a genus. And by our statement: 'exits the essence' is excluded genus, differentia, and species, for they are not external to it, rather the first two are parts of it and the third is its complete [essence]. And by our statement: 'and is true... etc.' is excluded the property, for although it exits the essence, it is true only of it. And know that the common accident is of two types: the first: necessary, like 'breathing by potentiality'. And the second: separable, like 'breathing by actuality'.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines the common accident (al-'arad al-'amm). The author begins by stating that 'arad here means common, not special. He defines it as what is external to the essence (al-mahiyya) and is predicated of that essence and of other essences. Example: 'moving' is true of both man and horse. He then analyses the definition word by word. The word 'ma' (what) refers to the universal that covers all five universals, so it is a genus. The first part ('exits the essence') excludes the universals that are internal to the essence: genus (part), differentia (part), and species (the whole essence). The second part ('and is true of it and others') excludes property (khass), which is true only of one species. Finally, he divides common accident into two: necessary (lazim), which is inseparable like 'breathing by potentiality', and separable (mufariq), which can be absent like 'breathing by actuality'.

Key Terms
لازم
مفارق
قوة
فعل

A) Laughing (al-dahik)

C) Writing (al-kitaba)
D) Standing (al-qiyam)

Key Takeaway
Necessary common accidents are inseparable from the essence, while separable ones are not; this distinction is crucial for stable legal analogies.

The Definition of Species (Naw')
Author defines species and distinguishes it from genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish species (naw') from genus (jins) based on the condition of gathering in the question.

Core Idea
Species answers 'what is it?' for many, even if only one is asked.

In the previous lesson, we learned about genus. Now we turn to species, another of the five universals. The author defines species and then clarifies a key difference: unlike genus, species does not require multiple individuals to be mentioned in the question. Understanding this distinction is essential for precise definitions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Locate the term being defined (نوع) and the definition: 'what is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many individuals agreeing in reality'.
This is a real definition (hadd haqiqi) that captures the essence.
2
Examine the example
The author gives 'man' (الإنسان) as an example, showing it applies to Zayd and Amr. Note that even if asked about Zayd alone, 'man' is still a valid answer.
This illustrates that species does not require multiple individuals in the question.
3
Analyze the key condition: 'true of many' (صدق على كثيرين)
Understand that 'true of many' means the universal can be predicated of many individuals, not that the question must mention many. The capability of being predicated of many is sufficient.
This is the defining feature of species compared to other universals.
4
Contrast species with genus
The author explicitly states that unlike genus, species does not require the individuals to be gathered in the question. For genus, the question must include multiple species (e.g., 'what are man and horse?') to be a genus.
This distinction is crucial for correctly classifying universals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (نَوْعٌ) هُوَ: مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ مُتَّفِقِينَ بِالْحَقِيقَةِ كَالْإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ، فَإِذَا قِيلَ: زَيْدٌ وَعَمْرٌو مَا هُوَ؟ صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ، بَلْ لَوْ قِيلَ: زَيْدٌ مَا هُوَ؟ صَلُحَ لِذَلِكَ، فَيُقَالَ: إِنْسَانٌ لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ هُنَا بِصِدْقِهِ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ حَمْلُهُ عَلَيْهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجْتَمِعْ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِخِلَافِ صِدْقِ الْجِنْسِ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ فِيمَا مَرَّ فَإِنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ جَمْعِهَا فِي ذَلِكَ.
His statement: 'species' it is: what is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many individuals agreeing in reality, like 'man', for it is true in answer to 'what is it?' of many. So when it is said: Zayd and Amr, what are they? it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that upon what was mentioned in the question. Rather, even if it is said: Zayd, what is he? it is suitable for that, so it is said: man, because the intended meaning here of its being true of many is its predication of them, even if they are not gathered in the question, unlike the truth of genus of many in what has passed, for it is necessary to gather them in that.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines species (naw'). The author states that species is what is said in answer to 'what is it?' (ma huwa) about many individuals that share the same reality (haqiqa). Example: 'man' is true of Zayd, 'Amr, etc. He explains that the definition does not require multiple individuals to be mentioned together in the question. Even if asked about a single individual, 'man' is suitable. This is because the condition 'true of many' means the universal can be predicated of many, not that the question must include many. This distinguishes species from genus: in the case of genus (as previously discussed in the differentia section), the genus requires the individuals to be gathered in the question (e.g., 'what are man and horse?') for it to be a genus. Thus, species is more flexible—it can be predicated even in a singular question.

Key Terms
نوع (naw'): Species: the universal that answers 'what is it?' for multiple individuals of the same essence; here it is distinguished from genus by not requiring the individuals to be gathered in the question. [Note: Stable definition across the tradition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It answers 'what is it?' for many individuals of the same reality, even if asked about one person.
B) It is a genus for animals.
C) It is a differentia for rational beings.
D) It is an accident of body.

Key Takeaway
Species is the universal that answers 'what is it?' for many individuals of the same reality, and it does not require the individuals to be gathered in the question, unlike genus.

Genus and Differentia: The First Two Universals
Author lists the five universals and defines genus and differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish genus from differentia and identify them in a given definition.

Core Idea
Genus answers 'what is it?' while differentia answers 'what sort of thing is it?'.

The five universals are the building blocks of all definitions. In this passage, al-Bajuri defines the first two: genus and differentia. Understanding their distinction is crucial for constructing accurate definitions in Islamic sciences like fiqh and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five universals
Read the first sentence and note the five terms: jins, fasl, arad, naw, khaas. Understand that these are the categories used to analyze concepts.
Memorize the list for quick recall.
2
Extract the definition of genus
Find the part where al-Bajuri explains when a term is called 'jins'. It is when it is used in answer to 'ma huwa?' (what is it?) for multiple things differing in reality, like 'animal' for human and horse.
The key is the question 'ma huwa?'.
3
Extract the definition of differentia
Locate the definition of 'fasl'. It is what is predicated in answer to 'ayyu shay huwa?' (what sort of thing is it?) and distinguishes the species.
Differentia gives the distinguishing characteristic.
4
Analyze the shifting consideration
Notice al-Bajuri's remark that the same term can be genus in one context and differentia in another. For example, 'animal' is genus for human and horse, but could be a differentia for something else. Reflect on why this flexibility exists.
This prevents rigid thinking about definitions.
5
Apply to a real example
Take the definition of 'salah' (prayer) as 'specific actions and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'. Identify the genus (actions and words) and the differentia (beginning with takbir and ending with taslim).
Verify that the genus answers 'what is it?' and the differentia answers 'what sort of thing is it?'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالكُلْيَاتُ خَمْسَةٌ دُونَ انْتِقَاصُ جِنْسُ، وَفَصْلٌ، عَرَضَ، نَوْعٌ، وَخَاصٌ. الباجوري : - وَإِذَا وَقَعَ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟»؛ كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ : الإِنْسَانُ وَالفَرَسُ مَا هُوَ؟»، فَقُلْتَ: «حَيَوَانٌ»، كَانَ جِنْساً ، فَهُوَ فَصْلٌ بِاعْتِبَارِ، وَجِنْسُ بِاعْتِبَارٍ آخَرَ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
And the universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, and property. Al-Bajuri: - And if it occurs in response to 'what is it?', like when it is said: 'Human and horse, what are they?' and you say: 'Animal', it is genus. Then it is differentia by one consideration and genus by another consideration, so let it be contemplated.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage begins by enumerating the five universals (al-kulliyyāt al-khamsah): genus (jins), differentia (faṣl), accident (ʿaraḍ), species (nawʿ), and property (khāṣṣ). Then al-Bajuri's commentary defines genus and differentia. Genus is what is predicated in answer to the question 'what is it?' (mā huwa) when applied to many differing in reality (mukhtalifīn bi-l-ḥaqīqah). For example, when asked about human and horse, one answers 'animal' – that is genus. Differentia, on the other hand, is what is predicated in answer to the question 'what sort of thing is it?' (ayyu shayʾ huwa). However, al-Bajuri notes that the same term can be genus by one consideration and differentia by another, as in the case of 'animal' relative to human and horse (genus) but also a differentia relative to something else if it serves to distinguish. He advises careful reflection on this.

Key Terms
جنس
فصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Genus answers the question 'what is it?' for many differing things, while differentia answers 'what sort of thing is it?' and distinguishes them—and the same term can serve both roles depending on context.

The Five Universals and Their Logical Roles
Al-Bajuri defines the five universals by their roles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify each of the five universals according to whether it answers 'what is it?' or 'which thing is it?' and whether it applies to many that agree or differ in essence.

Core Idea
The five universals are tools to answer two questions: 'what is it?' and 'which thing is it?'.

In this passage, al-Bajuri lays out the five universals—genus, differentia, accident, species, property—and shows how they are distinguished by two key factors: the kind of question they answer and the scope of their application. Understanding this classification is essential for precise definition and logical predication in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
List the five universals
Find the five terms: jins (genus), fasl (differentia), 'arad (accident), naw' (species), and khassa (property). They are all universals applying to many.
Accident here is not the philosophical accident but a universal predicable.
2
Identify the two questions
The passage uses 'ma huwa?' (what is it?) and 'ayyu shay' huwa?' (which thing is it?). Without relation to 'what?', the common accident applies. With that relation, differentia and property answer 'which thing is it?'.
3
Understand the phrase 'to many' (ala kathirin)
By adding 'to many', we get the definition (hadd). The definition is a universal that applies to many individuals. This distinguishes it from singular concepts.
The definition here is the logical definition, not the term 'definition' in the sense of hadd tamm.
4
Restrict 'to many' with 'agreeing in essence'
By restricting 'to many' with 'those agreeing in essence' (al-muttafiqin bi al-haqiqa), we get the genus. Genus applies to many that differ in specific essence (e.g., animal applies to humans and horses).
The genus answers 'what is it?' but for things differing in essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكليات خمسة دون انتقاص: جنس، فصل، عرض، نوع، خاص. بقطع النظر عن الإضافة لـ«ما»: العرض العام؛ لما تقدم. وبالنظر لها: الفصل، والخاصة؛ فإن كلا منهما يصدق في جواب أي شيء هو؟ وبقولنا: «على كثيرين»: الحد؛ لما مر. وبالتقييد بـ«المتفقين بالحقيقة»: الجنس؛ فإنه يصدق في جواب ما هو؟ على المختلفين بالحقيقة. فإن قيل: حقيقة كل من زيد، وعمرو مركبة من: الإنسان، والتشخص المختص به الذي لا يشاركه فيه غيره، فهما مختلفان بالحقيقة. أجيب: بأن المراد بـ(الحقيقة) هنا: الحقيقة النوعية كـ: حيوان ناطق، لا الشخصية كـ: الإنسان، والتشخص، ولا شك أنهما متفقان في الأولى؛ إذ يصدق على كل منهما أنه حيوان ناطق، وإن لم يتفقا في الثانية، والنوع المعرّف بما ذكر إنما هو النوع الحقيقي، وأما الإضافي فهو: ما صدق في جواب ما هو؟ على كثيرين، وقد اندرج تحت جنس، وبينه وبين النوع الحقيقي (١): عموم وخصوص من وجه، فيجتمعان في نحو «الإنسان»، وينفرد الإضافي في نحو «الحيوان»، والحقيقي في نحو «النقطة».
The universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, property. Without consideration of the relation to 'what?': the common accident; due to what preceded. With consideration of it: the differentia and the property; for each of them answers the question 'which thing is it?'. By our saying 'to many': the definition; due to what passed. By restricting with 'those agreeing in essence': the genus; for it answers the question 'what is it?' about those differing in essence. If it is said: The essence of each of Zayd and 'Amr is composed of the human and the special individuality that no other shares with him, so they differ in essence. It is answered: That by 'essence' here is meant the specific essence like 'rational animal', not the personal like 'human' and 'individuality'. No doubt they agree in the first, for each of them is described as 'rational animal', even if they do not agree in the second. And the species defined by what was mentioned is only the true species. As for the additional species, it is that which answers 'what is it?' concerning many, being included under a genus. Between it and the true species there is general and special from a perspective: they meet in something like 'human', and the additional is unique in something like 'animal', and the true is unique in something like 'point'.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the five universals (genus, differentia, accident, species, property) as commonly used in Islamic logic. The author, al-Bajuri, explains how these terms are distinguished by considering whether they answer the question 'what is it?' (ma huwa?) or 'which thing is it?' (ayyu shay' huwa?), and whether they apply to many individuals that are the same in essence or different. He starts by stating the five universals. Then he explains that without considering the relation to the question 'what?', the common accident applies. With that relation, the differentia and property each answer 'which thing is it?'. By adding 'to many', we get the definition (hadd). By restricting 'to many' with 'agreeing in essence', we get the genus, which applies to things differing in essence. An objection is raised: the essence of any two individuals like Zayd and 'Amr is composed of species (human) and individuating factor, so they differ in essence. The answer distinguishes between specific essence (haqiqa naw'iyya) and personal essence (haqiqa shakhsiyya). The species defined here is the true species (naw' haqiqi), which applies to many agreeing in specific essence. Then the additional species (naw' idafi) is introduced: it applies to many, is under a genus, and has a relationship of general-and-special from a perspective with the true species. Examples: both apply to 'human'; additional species alone to 'animal'; true species alone to 'point'. This passage sets the framework for understanding predication in logic.

Key Terms
الجنس
الفصل
العرض
النوع
الخاصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Accident and property
D) Genus and differentia

Key Takeaway
The five universals are classified by the type of question they answer and the agreement or difference in essence among their instances.

The Objection on Essence and the True vs. Additional Species
Al-Bajuri resolves an objection and distinguishes true vs. additional species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the true species (al-naw' al-haqiqi) from the additional species (al-naw' al-idafi) and explain why individuals like Zayd and 'Amr share a specific essence.

Core Idea
True species answers 'what is it?' for those sharing the same specific essence; additional species is relative to a genus.

Al-Bajuri anticipates a crucial objection: if each individual has a unique composition of species and individuation, how can they share an essence? He responds by distinguishing specific essence (haqiqa naw'iyya) from personal essence (haqiqa shakhsiyya). This leads to the distinction between the true species and the additional species, refining the definition of 'species'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector says: Zayd and 'Amr each have an essence composed of 'human' (species) and a unique individuating factor. Therefore they differ in essence, contradicting the definition of genus (which applies to many differing in essence).
The objection targets the claim that genus applies to many differing in essence.
2
Grasp the response: specific vs. personal essence
Al-Bajuri responds that 'essence' here means specific essence (haqiqa naw'iyya), not personal essence (haqiqa shakhsiyya). Both Zayd and 'Amr share the specific essence 'rational animal', even though their personal essences differ.
This salvages the definition of genus.
3
Define the true species
The true species (al-naw' al-haqiqi) is a universal that answers 'what is it?' and applies to many agreeing in specific essence. Example: 'human' for Zayd and 'Amr.
This is the standard definition of species.
4
Define the additional species
The additional species (al-naw' al-idafi) answers 'what is it?' for many, but it is under a genus. It is broader than the true species. Example: 'animal' relative to 'human'.
It is called 'additional' because it adds a broader category beyond the true species.
5
Compare the two species
The true and additional species have a relationship of general and special from a perspective. They meet in 'human' (both apply), the additional is unique in 'animal', and the true is unique in 'point' (since a point is not under a genus like animal).
This shows they are not the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكليات خمسة دون انتقاص: جنس، فصل، عرض، نوع، خاص. بقطع النظر عن الإضافة لـ«ما»: العرض العام؛ لما تقدم. وبالنظر لها: الفصل، والخاصة؛ فإن كلا منهما يصدق في جواب أي شيء هو؟ وبقولنا: «على كثيرين»: الحد؛ لما مر. وبالتقييد بـ«المتفقين بالحقيقة»: الجنس؛ فإنه يصدق في جواب ما هو؟ على المختلفين بالحقيقة. فإن قيل: حقيقة كل من زيد، وعمرو مركبة من: الإنسان، والتشخص المختص به الذي لا يشاركه فيه غيره، فهما مختلفان بالحقيقة. أجيب: بأن المراد بـ(الحقيقة) هنا: الحقيقة النوعية كـ: حيوان ناطق، لا الشخصية كـ: الإنسان، والتشخص، ولا شك أنهما متفقان في الأولى؛ إذ يصدق على كل منهما أنه حيوان ناطق، وإن لم يتفقا في الثانية، والنوع المعرّف بما ذكر إنما هو النوع الحقيقي، وأما الإضافي فهو: ما صدق في جواب ما هو؟ على كثيرين، وقد اندرج تحت جنس، وبينه وبين النوع الحقيقي (١): عموم وخصوص من وجه، فيجتمعان في نحو «الإنسان»، وينفرد الإضافي في نحو «الحيوان»، والحقيقي في نحو «النقطة».
The universals are five without deficiency: genus, differentia, accident, species, property. Without consideration of the relation to 'what?': the common accident; due to what preceded. With consideration of it: the differentia and the property; for each of them answers the question 'which thing is it?'. By our saying 'to many': the definition; due to what passed. By restricting with 'those agreeing in essence': the genus; for it answers the question 'what is it?' about those differing in essence. If it is said: The essence of each of Zayd and 'Amr is composed of the human and the special individuality that no other shares with him, so they differ in essence. It is answered: That by 'essence' here is meant the specific essence like 'rational animal', not the personal like 'human' and 'individuality'. No doubt they agree in the first, for each of them is described as 'rational animal', even if they do not agree in the second. And the species defined by what was mentioned is only the true species. As for the additional species, it is that which answers 'what is it?' concerning many, being included under a genus. Between it and the true species there is general and special from a perspective: they meet in something like 'human', and the additional is unique in something like 'animal', and the true is unique in something like 'point'.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the five universals (genus, differentia, accident, species, property) as commonly used in Islamic logic. The author, al-Bajuri, explains how these terms are distinguished by considering whether they answer the question 'what is it?' (ma huwa?) or 'which thing is it?' (ayyu shay' huwa?), and whether they apply to many individuals that are the same in essence or different. He starts by stating the five universals. Then he explains that without considering the relation to the question 'what?', the common accident applies. With that relation, the differentia and property each answer 'which thing is it?'. By adding 'to many', we get the definition (hadd). By restricting 'to many' with 'agreeing in essence', we get the genus, which applies to things differing in essence. An objection is raised: the essence of any two individuals like Zayd and 'Amr is composed of species (human) and individuating factor, so they differ in essence. The answer distinguishes between specific essence (haqiqa naw'iyya) and personal essence (haqiqa shakhsiyya). The species defined here is the true species (naw' haqiqi), which applies to many agreeing in specific essence. Then the additional species (naw' idafi) is introduced: it applies to many, is under a genus, and has a relationship of general-and-special from a perspective with the true species. Examples: both apply to 'human'; additional species alone to 'animal'; true species alone to 'point'. This passage sets the framework for understanding predication in logic.

Key Terms
النوع الحقيقي
النوع الإضافي
الحقيقة النوعية
الحقيقة الشخصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they have the same personal essence
B) Because they share the same specific essence (rational animal)
C) Because each is composed of different components
D) Because they are both individuals

Key Takeaway
The true species is defined by specific essence, not personal essence, and the additional species broadens the scope under a genus.

Ranks of the Additional Species (Naw' Idafi)
Al-Bajuri enumerates the four ranks of the additional species with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given universal as a high, low, intermediate, or isolated additional species by analyzing its position in the hierarchical tree.

Core Idea
The rank of a species is determined by its position relative to other species above and below.

In this passage, al-Bajuri expands on the classification of the additional species (naw' idafi), which are universals that can be both species and genera depending on perspective. He begins by stating there are three ranks, then adds a fourth. Understanding these ranks is crucial for navigating the hierarchy of universals, a tool frequently used in Islamic logic and theology to organize concepts and definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four ranks
The passage lists four ranks: high (no species above, species below), low (no species below, species above), intermediate (both above and below), and isolated (neither above nor below). Memorize these four categories.
The isolated species is a later addition; some earlier logicians only recognized three.
2
Apply the examples
The passage gives examples: 'body' (high), 'human' (low), 'animal' (intermediate), and 'intellect' (isolated). For each, verify that it satisfies the definition by checking what species are above and below it in the Porphyrian tree.
3
Understand the isolated species caveat
The isolated species is exemplified by 'intellect' only if one accepts that intellect is a species with no higher genus and no lower species. This is a philosophical position, not universally accepted, showing that classification can be theory-dependent.
In Islamic philosophy, 'intellect' ('aql) is often considered a separate substance with no species under it, hence isolated.
4
Test with new examples
Try classifying 'plant', 'stone', 'angel' using the same criteria. For instance, 'plant' is below 'body' and above 'tree', so it is an intermediate species. This step internalizes the method.
Use examples from Islamic cosmology or theology to make the exercise relevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مراتب النوع الإضافي ثلاثة: (1) - النوع العالي، وهو: ما لا أنواع فوقه، وتحته الأنواع كـ: «الجسم». (٢) - والنوع السافل، وهو: ما لا نوع تحته، وفوقه الأنواع كـ: «الإنسان». (۳) - والنوع المتوسط، وهو: ما فوقه نوع، وتحته نوع كـ: «الحيوان». (٤) - وبقي رابع، وهو: النوع المنفرد، وهو ما لا نوع فوقه، ولا نوع تحته، ويمثل له بـ«العقل»؛ بناءً على نوعيته.
Know that the ranks of the additional species are three: (1) The high species, which is that which has no species above it, and under it are species, like 'body'. (2) The low species, which is that which has no species under it, and above it are species, like 'human'. (3) The intermediate species, which is that above which is a species and under which is a species, like 'animal'. (4) And a fourth remains, which is the isolated species, and it is that which has no species above it nor species under it, and it is exemplified by 'intellect', based on its being a species.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the additional species (naw' idafi) into four ranks by al-Bajuri. He initially says there are three, then adds a fourth. The high species (naw' 'ali) has no species above it but has species under it, like 'body' (jism) which is a genus for many species (e.g., animal, plant, mineral). The low species (naw' safil) has no species under it but has species above it, like 'human' (insan) which is a species with no subspecies (though individuals below). The intermediate species (naw' mutawassit) has both a species above and below, like 'animal' which is a species of 'body' and a genus for 'human', 'horse', etc. The fourth is the isolated species (naw' munfarid) which has no species above or below, exemplified by 'intellect' ('aql) according to the philosophical view that it is a species with no genus above it (or no species under it). This classification helps in understanding the hierarchy of universals in Porphyry's tree, a common tool in Islamic logic.

Key Terms
النوع العالي
النوع السافل
النوع المتوسط
النوع المنفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Low species

D) Isolated species

Key Takeaway
The additional species is classified into four ranks based on whether it has species above, below, both, or neither; this hierarchy is fundamental for understanding definitions and classifications in Islamic logic.

The Special Property (Khas): Definition and Example
Author defines 'special property' (khas) and illustrates with the example 'laughing' for humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a 'khas' (special property) in a definition and distinguish it from 'fasl' (differentia).

Core Idea
A special property answers 'what is it?' in terms of accident, not essence.

In the system of the five universals, we already learned about the differentia (fasl) which distinguishes a species by its essence. Now we encounter another distinguisher: the special property (khas). This universal also differentiates a thing, but not by its essence—only by an accident that belongs to it uniquely. The passage defines it precisely and gives a classic example that has been used for centuries in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'khas' (special property). Note the orthographic note: it is written without the final 'ha' (common in Arabic) and with a lightened 'sad' due to poetic necessity. That is a side detail; the core is the definition.
2
Understand the question it answers
The definition says: 'what is true in answer to 'what is it in its accident?'' So a khas is a property that can be truthfully said of a thing when you consider it under its accident, not under its essence. Ask yourself: what does 'in its accident' mean? It means considering the thing with respect to its accidental attributes.
The commentary explains: 'in the state of his being subsumed under his accident'.
3
Extract the definition
From the passage: a khas is a universal that applies to a thing in answer to the question 'what is it in its accident?'. It is a predicate that does not reveal the essence but an accidental property.
4
Apply the example: 'laughing' (al-dahik) for humans
The passage gives the example: when we ask 'what is the differentiator of man in his accident?' (i.e., considering man under his accidental properties), the answer is 'laughing'. This shows that 'laughing' is a khas of man: it distinguishes humans from other animals, but it is not part of the essence (humans could exist without laughing, though in reality they are the only ones who do).
This example is stable in the tradition and helps distinguish khas from fasl (e.g., 'rational' is a fasl because it answers 'what is it in its essence?' and is essential).
5
Distinguish khas from fasl and other universals
Khas is like a differentia but accidental. It is a type of 'khassa' (property) that is peculiar to a species. While differentia (fasl) answers 'what is it in its essence?', khas answers 'what is it in its accident?'. Recognizing this distinction is crucial for correct definition and classification in Islamic sciences.
Common misunderstanding: confusing khas with fasl. Remember: fasl = essential, khas = accidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (وَخَاص) بِحَذْفِ الهَاءِ ، وَتَخْفِيفِ الصَّادِ؛ لِلضَّرُورَةِ. وَهِيَ : مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ ؟ »؛ كَـ: «الصَّاحِكِ»، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ: مُمَيِّزُ الإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ؟ أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مُنْدَرِجاً فِي عَرَضِهِ، صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: «ضَاحِدٌ».
His statement: 'and khas' [is written] with the omission of the ha and with tashdid of the sad, due to poetic necessity. And it (khas) is: what is true in answer to 'what is it in its accident?', like 'laughing', for it is true in answer to that. If it is said: 'What is the differentiator of man in his accident?' i.e., in the state of his being subsumed under his accident, it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that, according to what was mentioned in the question, by saying: 'laughing'.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth universal: 'khas' (special property). It begins by noting that the word 'khas' is written without the final ha (i.e., خاص not خاصة) and with a single sad (not شديد? Actually 'takhfif al-sad' means without shaddah? Wait: 'wa tashdid al-sad' in the text says 'tashdid'? The OCR says 'وَتَخْفِيفِ الصَّادِ' which means 'and making the sad light' (i.e., without shaddah). But the phrase 'لِلضَّرُورَةِ' refers to poetic meter. Then the definition: 'khas' is whatever is true in answer to 'what is it in its accident?'. The example is 'al-dahik' (the laughable or the one who laughs). The explanation: if one asks 'what is the differentiator of man in his accident?' (i.e., considering man as subsumed under his accidents), the answer is 'laughing'. This shows that 'khas' is a predicate that does not give the essence but an accident peculiar to the species. The commentary then explains the structure of the question: 'what is it in its accident?' means 'what is it while being subsumed under its accident?' The answer 'laughing' is valid because it is an inherent property (khassa) of man, not a differentia (fasl).

Defining the Fifth Universal: Property (خاص)
Al-Bajuri defines the fifth universal (خاص) and gives an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of khass (property) in Islamic logic and distinguish it from other universals by its interrogative test.

Core Idea
Property is the universal that answers 'what is it in its accident?' and is coextensive with the species.

In this passage, al-Bajuri defines the fifth universal, al-khass (property), and illustrates it with the example of laughter for man. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sharpens the distinction between property and other predicable terms like genus and accident. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply this definition to any universal in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the word 'خاص' in the Arabic and note its orthographic peculiarities (deletion of ha, lightening of sad). This guards against confusion with other terms.
This is due to poetic necessity (ضرورة).
2
Analyze the definition formula
The definition is 'ما صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ?' meaning 'that which is true in answer to the question: what thing is it in its accident?' Notice the phrase 'في عرضه' (in its accident). This is the distinctive interrogative frame for property.
Contrast with genus which answers 'what is it in its essence?' (في جوهره).
3
Apply the definition to an example
The commentator gives 'الضاحك' (the laughing one) as a property of man. If someone asks 'What is the distinguisher of man in its accident?' The answer is 'laughter'. Verify that this answer is true for all and only humans.
The example shows that property is coextensive (مساوِ) with the species.
4
Examine the logical note about 'ما'
The commentator explains that the relative pronoun 'ما' in the definition refers to a universal that encompasses all universals, making it a genus (جنس). This means that 'property' as a universal is itself a genus for the five universals? Actually, the text says 'ما' is the universal covering all universals, so it is a genus. This is a subtle point: the definition applies to every universal that is a property.
This clarifies the scope of the definition.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (وَخَاص) بِحَذْفِ الهَاءِ ، وَتَخْفِيفِ الصَّادِ؛ لِلضَّرُورَةِ. وَهِيَ : مَا صَدَقَ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ ؟ »؛ كَـ: «الصَّاحِكِ»، فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ: مُمَيِّزُ الإِنْسَانِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي عَرَضِهِ؟ أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِهِ مُنْدَرِجاً فِي عَرَضِهِ، صَلُحَ لِأَنْ يُحْمَلَ فِي جَوَابِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ فِي السُّؤَالِ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ: «ضَاحِدٌ». وَمَا» : وَاقِعَةٌ عَلَى الكُلِّيِّ الشَّامِلِ لِجَمِيعِ الكُلْيَّاتِ، فَهِيَ جِنْسٌ
His statement: (and property) with the deletion of the ha and the lightening of the sad due to necessity. And it is: that which is true in answer to 'what thing is it in its accident?' like 'the laughing one', for it is true in answer to that. For if it is said: 'The distinguisher of man, what thing is it in its accident?' i.e., while being included in its accident, it is suitable to be predicated in answer to that as mentioned in the question, by saying: 'a laughter'. And 'ma' is a relative pronoun applying to the universal that encompasses all universals, so it is a genus.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth universal known as 'خاص' (property) from the matn 'al-Kulliyat al-Khamsah'. The commentator explains that 'خاص' is written with a silent ha and a lightened sad due to poetic necessity. Its definition is: a universal that applies to the subject in answer to the question 'what thing is it in its accident?' For example, 'the laughing one' is a property of humans because it answers the question 'what distinguishes man in its accident?' The pronoun 'ما' in the definition refers to the universal that covers all universals, making it a genus (i.e., it is a genus for the other universals in a certain sense). This clarification guards against confusing property with accident or other universals.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A universal that is true in answer to 'what is it in its accident?' like laughter for man. [Note: In later texts, khass is often explicitly divided into necessary (lazim) and separable (mufariq), which is not mentioned here.]

The Fivefold Division of Substance by Philosophers
The commentator reports the philosophers' fivefold division of substance and the Ahl al-Sunnah's alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five types of substance identified by the philosophers and explain the logical relation of each type (genus, species, individual).

Core Idea
Substance is not a simple category; philosophers divided it into five distinct quiddities.

The passage from al-Bannani's commentary reports the philosophers' detailed classification of substance (jawhar). This classification is a perfect example of how the five universals (kulliyat khams) apply to a concept: 'jawhar' is a genus that subdivides into species (form, hyle, body, soul, intellect). Understanding this helps us appreciate the scope of logical analysis in Islamic metaphysics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being divided. In the passage, it is 'al-jawhar' (الجوهر). It is defined as a quiddity that when existing externally is not in a subject.
2
Extract the division criterion
The philosophers divide substance based on whether it is a form, a substrate (hyle), composite of both, or neither. Notice the logical operation: a genus is divided by differentiae.
The division uses the properties 'being a form' and 'being a substrate' as differentia.
3
List the five types
From the division, we get: (i) form (sura), (ii) hyle (hayula), (iii) body (jism) = composite, (iv) soul (nafs) = abstract that manages body, (v) intellect ('aql) = abstract unrelated to body.
Each type is a species under the genus 'jawhar'.
4
Assess the Ahl al-Sunnah position
The commentator notes that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, only the indivisible atom (al-fard) and the body (al-jism) are recognized, rejecting the other divisions.
This shows how creedal commitments can affect logical taxonomy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبابي المشخّصة لا بالفصول، وقدَّرنا أنَّ الجوهر المجرَّد جنس له، وذهب الإمام إلى أنَّه جنس تحته أنواع مختلفة بفصول لا نعلمها، فعلى هذا القول يكون جنساً منفرداً على تقدير أنَّ الجوهر المجرَّد ليس جنساً له، بل هو عَرَضُ عام له. أفاده الصَّبَّان. المادة وعلائقها . وفي البناني: أنَّ الفلاسفة قسَّموا الجوهر وهو ماهيَّةٌ إذا وجدت في الخارج كانت لا في موضوع إلى خمسة أقسام؛ لأنَّه إما حال ويسمى: «الصُّورة»، وإمَّا محل وهو : «الهَيُولَى»، وإِمَّا مركّب منهما وهو : «الجسم»، أم لا حال ولا محلُّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان؛ لأنَّه إما أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التدبير وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلّق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم : جوهر مجرَّد. واختلفوا في جنس العقول العشرة، وهو المجرَّد عن المادة وعلائقها، هل هو مندرج تحت الجوهر أم لا؟ واختلفوا في العقول العشرة : هل اختلفت بالحقيقة والفصول، فتكون أنواعاً والعقل جنسها، أو بالعوارض والخواص، فيكون العقل نوعاً لها وهي أفراده؟ ثمَّ على القول بأنَّه تحت الجوهر وأنَّه من أقسامه كان نوعيّاً إضافيا على كلِّ مِنَ القولين الأخيرين، وعلى القول بأنَّه ليس من أقسامه، وأنَّ الجوهر ينقسم إلى: الحال، والمحلّ، والمركب منهما فقط، فعلى أنَّه جنس يكون جنساً منفرداً، وعلى أنه نوع يكون نوعاً منفرداً كالنُّقطة . والحُقُّ عند أهل السُّنَّة رضي الله تعالى عنهم : أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلا فهو الجسم وأنكروا جميع ما عدا ذلك . اهـ باختصار، وقد بيّن العلامة الصَّبَّان العقول العشرة وغيرها كالأفلاك، فراجعه.
Al-Anbabi: [the property is] specified not by differentiae, and we estimated that the abstract substance is a genus for it, and the Imam went that it is a genus under which are different types with differentiae we do not know. So on this view it becomes a separate genus on the assumption that the abstract substance is not a genus for it, rather it is a common accident for it. Al-Sabban informed us of this. Matter and its relations. And in al-Bannani: the philosophers divided substance, which is a quiddity that when found externally is not in a subject, into five divisions: because it is either a form (called 'form') or a substrate (called 'hyle'), or composed of both (called 'body'), or neither form nor substrate (which is the abstract), and in it are two divisions: because either it relates to the body as a managing relation (the soul) or it does not relate to it (the intellect). So the intellect according to them is an abstract substance. And they disagreed about the genus of the ten intellects, which is abstracted from matter and its relations: is it included under substance or not? And they disagreed about the ten intellects: do they differ in reality and differentiae, thus being types with intellect as their genus, or by accidents and properties, thus intellect being a type for them and they are its individuals? Then on the view that it is under substance and one of its divisions, it is an additional type in both of the latter views. And on the view that it is not one of its divisions, and that substance is divided into form, substrate, and composite only, then if it is a genus it is a separate genus, and if it is a type it is a separate type like the point. And the truth according to the Ahl al-Sunnah, may God be pleased with them, is that substance if it does not accept division is the indivisible atom, otherwise it is the body, and they denied all that besides that. Summarized. And the scholar al-Sabban has explained the ten intellects and others like the celestial spheres, so refer to him.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the concept of substance and the intellect as a genus, likely within the commentary on the fifth universal. The commentator discusses the philosophical division of substance into five types: form (sura), hyle (hayula), body (jism), soul (nafs), and intellect ('aql). He then presents a debate about whether the ten intellects fall under the genus of substance or constitute a separate genus. The Ahl al-Sunnah position is clarified: they only recognize the indivisible atom and the body, rejecting the other divisions. This illustrates the application of logical categories to metaphysical entities.

الصورة
الهيولى
الجسم
النفس

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' fivefold division of substance demonstrates how the five universals are used to categorize metaphysical entities, and it contrasts with the Ash'ari position.

Is the Intellect a Genus? Logical Disagreement among Philosophers
The commentator explores the logical status of the intellect in relation to the ten intellects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two competing views on the logical status of the intellect ('aql) — whether it is a genus or a species — and the implications of each.

Core Idea
Whether the intellect is a genus or species depends on how we view the ten intellects — as differing by essence or by accident.

After presenting the fivefold division, the passage delves into a specific debate: what is the logical status of the intellect? Is it a genus that includes the ten intellects as species, or is it a species with the ten intellects as individuals? This debate illustrates the depth of logical analysis applied to metaphysical entities in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the debated term
The term under debate is 'al-'aql' (العقل), specifically in relation to the ten intellects (al-'uqul al-'ashara). The passage asks whether the intellect is included under the genus of substance or not.
2
Identify the two competing views
View 1: The ten intellects differ by reality and differentiae (haqiqa wa fusul), so they are species and 'aql is their genus. View 2: The ten intellects differ by accidents and properties (a'rad wa khawass), so they are individuals and 'aql is a species.
This is a classic application of the genus-species distinction.
3
Consider the additional layers
The passage also discusses the scenario where 'aql is under the genus of substance or not. If it is under substance, then in both views above, 'aql becomes a 'type' (naw') 'additional' (idafi). If it is not under substance, then substance is only form, hyle, body, and 'aql becomes either a separate genus or a separate species like the point (nuqta).
This shows the complexity of logical taxonomy.
4
Note the Ahl al-Sunnah position
The ultimate truth (al-haqq) according to Ahl al-Sunnah rejects the entire philosophical division, accepting only the indivisible atom (fard) and the body (jism).
This reminds us that logical analysis is not always accepted across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبابي المشخّصة لا بالفصول، وقدَّرنا أنَّ الجوهر المجرَّد جنس له، وذهب الإمام إلى أنَّه جنس تحته أنواع مختلفة بفصول لا نعلمها، فعلى هذا القول يكون جنساً منفرداً على تقدير أنَّ الجوهر المجرَّد ليس جنساً له، بل هو عَرَضُ عام له. أفاده الصَّبَّان. المادة وعلائقها . وفي البناني: أنَّ الفلاسفة قسَّموا الجوهر وهو ماهيَّةٌ إذا وجدت في الخارج كانت لا في موضوع إلى خمسة أقسام؛ لأنَّه إما حال ويسمى: «الصُّورة»، وإمَّا محل وهو : «الهَيُولَى»، وإِمَّا مركّب منهما وهو : «الجسم»، أم لا حال ولا محلُّ وهو المجرَّد، وفيه قسمان؛ لأنَّه إما أن يتعلَّق بالبدن تعلُّق التدبير وهو النَّفس، أو لا يتعلّق به وهو العقل، فالعقلُ على قولهم : جوهر مجرَّد. واختلفوا في جنس العقول العشرة، وهو المجرَّد عن المادة وعلائقها، هل هو مندرج تحت الجوهر أم لا؟ واختلفوا في العقول العشرة : هل اختلفت بالحقيقة والفصول، فتكون أنواعاً والعقل جنسها، أو بالعوارض والخواص، فيكون العقل نوعاً لها وهي أفراده؟ ثمَّ على القول بأنَّه تحت الجوهر وأنَّه من أقسامه كان نوعيّاً إضافيا على كلِّ مِنَ القولين الأخيرين، وعلى القول بأنَّه ليس من أقسامه، وأنَّ الجوهر ينقسم إلى: الحال، والمحلّ، والمركب منهما فقط، فعلى أنَّه جنس يكون جنساً منفرداً، وعلى أنه نوع يكون نوعاً منفرداً كالنُّقطة . والحُقُّ عند أهل السُّنَّة رضي الله تعالى عنهم : أنَّ الجوهر إن لم يقبل القسمة فهو الفرد، وإلا فهو الجسم وأنكروا جميع ما عدا ذلك . اهـ باختصار، وقد بيّن العلامة الصَّبَّان العقول العشرة وغيرها كالأفلاك، فراجعه.

The Three Genera and the Separate Genus
Al-Bajuri explains the first three types of genus and the separate genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify genera as proximate, remote, or intermediate, and identify the separate genus with an example.

Core Idea
Genus is relational: the same universal can be proximate to one species and remote to another.

In the study of the five universals, genus is not a single category. Al-Bajuri clarifies the three types of genus mentioned in the matn and adds a fourth, the separate genus, for completeness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three genera listed in the matn
Locate the phrase 'proximate, remote, or intermediate' and understand that these are relative to a given species.
2
Understand what is excluded
Al-Bajuri excludes common accident and differentia because they answer different questions: common accident does not answer 'what is it?' in itself, and differentia answers 'in its essence'.
3
Add the separate genus
The comment notes that without disregarding the separate genus, genus would be four; intellect is given as an example because it has no known species.
4
Apply the classification
Practice by taking a species like man and determining its proximate genus (animal), remote genus (living body), and intermediate genus (sentient body).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَوَّلُ ثَلَاثَةٌ بِلَا شَطَط: جنس قريبٌ، أَوْ بَعْيدٌ، أَوْ وَسَط 
الباجوري - وَخَرَجَ بِقَوْلِنَا : فِي جَوَابِ : بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الإِضَافَةِ لِـ «أَيُّ» : العَرَضُ العَامُ؛ لِمَا مَرَّ . - وَمَعَ النَّظَرِ لَهَا : الجِنْسُ، وَالنَّوْعُ ؛ لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ . وَبِقَوْلِنَا : فِي عَرَضِهِ» : الفَصْلُ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ فِي جَوَابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هُوَ فِي ذَاتِهِ؟»، كَمَا عَلِمْتَ . وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الخَاصَّةَ كَمَا تَكُونُ لِلنَّوْعِ تَكُونُ لِلجِنْسِ ؛ كَـ : المَاشِي، فَإِنَّهُ خَاصَّةٌ لِلحَيَوَانِ، وَلَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ كَوْنِهَا خَاصَّةٌ لِلجِنْسِ أَنْ تَكُونَ خَاصَّةٌ لِلنَّوْعِ، بِخِلَافِ العَكْسِ، فَكُلُّ خَاصَّةٍ لِلنَّوْعِ خَاصَّةٌ لِلجِنْسِ، وَلَا عَكْسَ. وَالخَاصَّةُ عَلَى نَوْعَيْنِ : (۱) - مُلَازِمَةٌ ؛ كَـ: «الصَّاحِكِ بِالقُوَّةِ». (٢) - وَمُفَارِقَةٌ ؛ كَـ : «الصَّاحِكِ بِالفِعْلِ». وَجَعْلُ الصَّاحِكِ مِنْ خَوَاصُ الإِنْسَانِ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ الحُكَمَاءُ مِنْ أَنَّ طَبْعَ المَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ لَا يَقْتَضِي الصَّحِكَ، كَمَا أَنَّهُ لَا يَقْتَضِي البُكَاءَ ، وَوُقُوعُ ذَلِكَ مِنْهُمْ - كَمَا وَرَدَ فِي بَعْضِ الآثَارِ - اتِّفَاقِيُّ، لَيْسَ بِاقْتِضَاءِ الطَّبْعِ ، وَبِهَذَا يُجَابُ عَمَّا حُكِيَ مِنْ أَنَّ النِّسْنَاسَ يَضْحَكُ إِذَا رَأَى أَوْ سَمِعَ مَا يَتَعَجَّبُ مِنْهُ، وَأَمَّا عَلَى مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ بَعْضُهُمْ مِنْ أَنَّ طَبْعَ المَلَائِكَةِ وَالجِنِّ يَقْتَضِي الضَّحِكَ، فَلَيْسَ «الصَّاحِكُ مِنْ خَوَاصُ الإِنْسَانِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لَهُمَا 
قَوْلُهُ : (وَأَوَّلُ) أي : الَّذِي هُوَ الجِنْسُ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (ثَلَاثَةٌ) أَيْ : بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ الجِنْسِ المُنْفَرِدِ ؛ لِعَدَمِ الظُّفْرِ بِمِثَالِهِ، وَإِلَّا فَمَعَ النَّظَرِ إِلَيْهِ يَكُونُ الجِنْسُ أَرْبَعَةٌ ، وَمَثَّلَ بَعْضُهُمْ لِلْجِنْسِ المُنْفَرِدِ بـ : «العَقْلِ»؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى جِنْسِيَّتِهِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : ( بِلَا شَطَط) أَيْ : بِلَا زِيَادَةٍ ؛ يَعْنِي: وَلَا نَقْصٍ، فَفِي كَلَامِهِ اكْتِفَاءُ . قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ : أَصْلُ قَوْلِهِ : بِلَا شَطَط» : لَا بِشَطَطِ (۱) ؛ لِأَنَّ حَقَّ حَرْفِ النَّفْيِ التَّقْدِيمُ عَلَى جَمِيعِ المَنْفِي (٢) ، وَهُوَ البَاءُ) مَعَ الشَّطَطِ الدَّالُ مَجْمُوعُهُمَا
And the first three without deviation: proximate genus, or remote, or intermediate. Al-Bajuri: And excluded by our saying 'in answer to' while disregarding the relation to 'which?' is the common accident, as has passed. And with the relation to it: genus and species, as has preceded. And by our saying 'in its accident' is the differentia, because it is true in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence?', as you know. And know that property, just as it is for the species, is also for the genus, like 'the walking one', for it is a property for animal. And it is not necessary from its being a property for the genus that it be a property for the species, contrary to the reverse. So every property of the species is a property of the genus, and not vice versa. And property is of two types: (1) necessary, like 'the laughing one potentially'; (2) separable, like 'the laughing one actually'. And making laughter one of the properties of humans is based on what the sages held: that the nature of angels and jinn does not necessitate laughter, just as it does not necessitate weeping. And its occurrence from them, as reported in some traditions, is accidental, not by natural necessity. And with this, one answers what is reported that the nisnas laughs when it sees or hears something that amazes it. But on the view of some that the nature of angels and jinn necessitates laughter, then 'the laughing one' is not among the properties of humans relative to them. His statement: (and the first) meaning that which is the genus. And his statement: (three) meaning by disregarding the separate genus due to inability to find an example of it; otherwise, considering it, genus would be four. And some gave as an example for the separate genus 'the intellect', based on its genus-ness. And his statement: (without deviation) meaning without increase, i.e., also without decrease. So in his statement there is sufficiency. Some said: the origin of his statement 'without deviation' is 'not with deviation', because the particle of negation has the right to precede all that is negated, and it is the 'ba' together with 'deviation' whose indication is their sum.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn stating that the first three (types of genus) are proximate, remote, and intermediate, without excess. Al-Bajuri explains that by our phrase 'in answer to' disregarding relation, the common accident is excluded; with relation, genus and species are included. By 'in its accident', the differentia is excluded because it answers 'in its essence'. He then discusses property: it can belong to both genus and species, with the example of 'walking' for animal. However, a property of genus is not necessarily a property of species. Property is divided into two: necessary (like potential laughter for humans) and separable (like actual laughter). The example of laughter as a property of humans is based on the view that angels and jinn do not naturally laugh; if they do, it is accidental. This answers objections about creatures like the nisnas laughing. Finally, al-Bajuri notes that the matn says 'first three' because the separate genus (like intellect) is excluded due to lack of clear example; without that, genus would be four. The phrase 'without deviation' means without excess or deficiency.

Key Terms
جنس قريب
جنس بعيد
جنس وسط
جنس منفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, what is the separate genus commonly exemplified by?
A) Animal
B) Intellect
C) Walking
D) Laughter

Key Takeaway
The genus classification is relative; the separate genus lacks known species.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
