مِنْ أَوَّلِيَّاتٍ مُشَاهَدَاتِ مُجَرَّبَاتٍ مُتَوَاتِرَاتِ وَحَدَسِيَّاتٍ، وَمَحْسُوسَاتِ؛ فَتِلْكَ جُمْلَةُ اليَقِينِياتِ. الباجوري: وَإِنَّمَا لَمْ يَذْكُرِ المُصَنِّفُ هَذَا القِسْمَ؛ لأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا تَكَلَّمَ عَنِ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ، وَهُوَ فِي الحَقِيقَةِ مِنَ النَّظَرِيَّاتِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَدَّهُ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ؛ لِأَنَّ قَضَايَاهُ لَمَّا كَانَتْ قِيَاسَاتُهَا لَا تَغِيبُ عَنِ الذِّهْنِ عِنْدَ تَصَوُّرِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ صَارَتْ كَأَنَّهَا ضَرُورِيَّةٌ، وَعُلِمَ مِنْ هَذَا أَنَّ العَدَدَ عَلَى كُلِّ سِتَّةٌ، فَتَفَطَنْ . قَوْلُهُ : (مُجَرَّبَاتٍ) هِيَ : مَا يُدْرِكُهَا العَقْلُ بِوَاسِطَةِ تَكْرَارٍ يُفيدُ اليَقِينَ»؛ كَقَوْلِكَ : «السَّقَمُونِيَا مُسْهَلَةٌ لِلصَّفْرَاءِ . وَكَلَامُ المُصَنِّفِ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى أَنَّ المُجَرَّبَاتِ مِنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ، وَجَعَلَهَا بَعْضُهُمْ مِنَ النَّظَرِيَّاتِ لِمُلَاحَظَةِ قِيَاسِ خَفِي (٢) ، وَجَعَلَهَا بَعْضُهُمْ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ وَالنَّظَرِيَّاتِ . (۲) هَذَا ؛ وَالمُتَّجِهُ الَّذِي دَرَجَ عَلَيْهِ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ العُلَمَاءِ - كَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ - أَنَّهَا مِنَ الظَّنِّيَّاتِ . قَوْلُهُ : (مُتَوَاتِرَاتِ هِيَ : مَا يُدْرِكُهَا العَقْلُ بِوَاسِطَةِ السَّمَاعِ عَنْ جَمْعِ يُؤْمَنُ تَوَاطُوْهُمْ عَلَى الكَذِبِ؛ كَقَوْلِكَ : سَيِّدُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ صلى الله عليه وسلم ظَهَرَتِ المُعْجِزَةُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ». وَالصَّحِيحُ : أَنَّهُ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ عَدَدٌ مَخْصُوص ، بَلِ المَدَارُ عَلَى كَوْنِ الْمُخْبِرِينَ يَمْتَنِعُ تَوَاطُوْهُمْ عَلَى الكَذِبِ، وَيَخْتَلِفٌ ذَلِكَ بِاخْتِلَافِ الوَقَائِعِ وَالأَحْوَالِ . وَكَلَامُ المُصَنِّفِ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى أَنَّ المُتَوَاتِرَاتِ مِنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ، وَجَعَلَهَا بَعْضُهُمْ مِنَ النَّظَرِيَّاتِ، وَجَعَلَهَا بَعْضُهُمْ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ وَالنَّظَرِيَّاتِ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَحَدَسِيَّاتٍ) هِيَ : القَضَايَا الَّتِي يُدْرِكُهَا العَقْلُ بِوَاسِطَةِ حَدَسٍ (۳) بَيْن يُفيدُ العِلْمَ»؛ كَقَوْلِكَ : «نُورُ القَمَرِ مُسْتَفَادٌ مِنْ نُورِ الشَّمْسِ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ . (۳) الشرشيمي: قوله : (بِوَاسِطَةِ حَدَسٍ ) أي : فناسب أن يسمَّى : (حدساً»، كما تقدَّم تقريره في أوَّل الكتاب. كتب ثانياً : قوله : (بِوَاسِطَةِ حَدَسٍ ) أي : مع التَّكرر ، فينبغي زيادة قيد في تعريف التجربيات في قولك : بِوَاسِطَةِ تَكْرَارٍ» أي: من غير حَدّس، وأيضاً المجرَّبات أمور اختياريَّةٌ بخلاف الحدسيات . وَكَلَامُ المُصَنِّفِ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى أَنَّ الحَدَسِيَّاتِ مِنَ الضَّرُورِيَّاتِ، وَجَعَلَهَا بَعْضُهُمْ مِنَ النَّظَرِيَّاتِ، وَالمُتَّجِهُ الَّذِي دَرَجَ عَلَيْهِ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ العُلَمَاءِ أَنَّهَا مِنَ الظَّنِّيَّاتِ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَمَحْسُوسَاتِ) هِيَ : مَا يُدْرِكُهَا العَقْلُ بِوَاسِطَةِ الحِسُ الظَّاهِرِ»؛ كَقَوْلِكَ : «الشَّمْسُ مُشْرِقَةٌ، وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ أَنَّ الفَرْقَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ المُشَاهَدَاتِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ اصْطَلَاحُ المُصَنِّفِ وَابْنِ الحَاجِبِ وَمَنْ وَافَقَهُمَا ، وَإِلَّا فَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا يُسَمَّى بِاسْمِ الآخَرِ . وَاعْتُرِضَ عَلَى التَّعْبِيرِ بِـ المَحْسُوسَاتِ بِأَنَّهَا جَمْعُ: «مَحْسُوس»، وَقِيَاسُ اسْمِ المَفْعُول : مُحَس» لَا مَحْسُوس»؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يُقَالُ: أَحَسَّ زَيْدٌ كَذَا ، أَوْ بِكَذَا، وَقِيَاسُ اسْمِ المَفْعُول مِنْهُ مَا ذُكِرَ. وَأُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يُتَوَسَّعُ فِي مِثْلِ ذَلِكَ. هَذَا ؛ وَذَهَبَ بَعْضُهُمْ إِلَى أَنَّ الحِسَّ لَا يُفِيدُ اليَقِينَ ; لِغَلَطِهِ فِي أُمُورٍ .
From first principles [awwaliyat], observations [mushahadat], empirical [mujarrabat], mutawatirat [recurrent reports], and intuitive [haddasiyyat], and sensed [mahsusat]; that is the totality of certainties. Al-Bajuri: The author [Ibn al-Hajib] did not mention this division [of theoretical] because he only spoke about necessary [daruriyyat], and it [theoretical] is in reality from theoretical [nazariyyat], but many considered it from necessary because its propositions' syllogisms do not disappear from the mind when the two extremes are conceived, so it becomes as if it were necessary. And from this it is known that the number [of types] is six, so pay attention. His statement: (Mujarrabat) are: what the intellect perceives by means of repetition that yields certainty, like your saying: 'Scammony is a purgative for yellow bile.' And the author's statement is based on [the view] that mujarrabat are from necessary, and some made them from theoretical due to observing a hidden syllogism, and some made them an intermediate between necessary and theoretical. (2) This; and the direction that many scholars followed – as some said – is that they are from probable [dhanniyyat]. His statement: (Mutawatirat) are: what the intellect perceives by means of hearing from a group whose collusion on lying is safe, like your saying: 'Our master Muhammad (peace be upon him) miracles appeared at his hands.' And the correct [view] is that no specific number is required, rather the criterion is that the informants are impossible to collude on lying, and that varies with the variation of events and circumstances. And the author's statement is based on [the view] that mutawatirat are from necessary, and some made them from theoretical, and some made them an intermediate between necessary and theoretical. His statement: (And haddasiyyat) are: the propositions that the intellect perceives by means of intuition that yields knowledge, like your saying: 'The light of the moon is derived from the light of the sun' as previously mentioned. (3) Al-Shirshimi: His statement (by means of intuition) i.e., so it is appropriate to call it 'intuitive' as was established at the beginning of the book. He wrote secondly: His statement (by means of intuition) i.e., with repetition, so a restriction should be added in the definition of empirical in your saying 'by means of repetition' i.e., without intuition, and also the empirical are matters of choice unlike the intuitive. And the author's statement is based on [the view] that haddasiyyat are from necessary, and some made them from theoretical, and the direction that many scholars followed is that they are from probable. His statement: (And mahsusat) are: what the intellect perceives by means of the external sense, like your saying: 'The sun is rising.' And it was previously mentioned that the difference between them and observations is only by the convention of the author and Ibn al-Hajib and those who agree with them, otherwise each is called by the name of the other. And an objection was raised against the expression 'mahsusat' that it is the plural of 'mahsus', and the analogical form of the passive participle is 'muhass' not 'mahsus', because one only says 'ahassa Zaydun kadha' or 'bi kadha', and the analogical passive participle from it is what was mentioned. And it was answered: that one may make an extension in such matters. This; and some went to the view that the sense does not yield certainty due to its error in some matters.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses the six types of certain premises (al-yaqiniyyat) as enumerated in the matn of al-Sullam: awwaliyat (first principles), mushahadat (observations), mujarrabat (empirical), mutawatirat (recurrent reports), haddasiyyat (intuitive), and mahsusat (sensed). The matn states that these six constitute the totality of certain propositions. The commentator (Bajuri) first explains why the author (Ibn al-Hajib) did not separately mention the theoretical certainty (nazariyyat) – because he was focusing on the necessary (daruriyyat), but in reality, those theoretical certainties are included because their syllogisms are so obvious that they appear necessary. Bajuri then notes that the total number is thus six. For each type, he provides a definition, an example, and then discusses the scholarly disagreement on whether each type is considered necessary (daruri), theoretical (nazari), or an intermediate (wasita), and in some cases, probable (dhanni). For mujarrabat, the example is 'Scammony is a purgative for yellow bile' – a medical generalization derived from repeated observation. For mutawatirat, the example is the miracle of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) known from widespread report. For haddasiyyat, the example is 'The light of the moon is derived from the light of the sun' – an intuitive conclusion based on a hidden cause. For mahsusat, the example is 'The sun is rising'. He also clarifies that the distinction between mushahadat and mahsusat is merely terminological for this author and Ibn al-Hajib. There is an objection about the word 'mahsusat' being linguistically irregular, answered by allowing linguistic extension. Finally, some doubt whether the senses yield certainty at all. Throughout, Bajuri presents the views without necessarily endorsing one; he notes that some scholars consider empirical, intuitive, and sense-based premises as only probable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of certain premise is exemplified by 'Scammony is a purgative for yellow bile'?
A) Awwaliyat (first principles)
B) Mutawatirat (recurrent reports)
C) Mujarrabat (empirical)
D) Haddasiyyat (intuitive)

Key Takeaway
The six types of certain premises provide the foundation for demonstrative knowledge in Islamic logic, each defined by its source of certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which type of certain premise each statement belongs to: (a) 'The whole is greater than the part.' (b) 'Muhammad (ﷺ) is the Messenger of Allah.' (c) 'Scammony purges yellow bile.' (d) 'The sun is rising.'
?
Construct a simple syllogism using at least one certain premise from each of two different types (e.g., awwaliyat and mutawatirat).
